    Translation

    The Complete Collection of Medical Texts from Ancient and Modern Times, Volume 292

    Jue Men (Gate of Observance)

    Huangdi Suwen (Huangdi's Simple Questions)

    Great Discussion on the Regulation of the Four Seasons and the Spirit

    In winter, during the three months, this is the time of closing and storing. The water freezes and the earth cracks; there should be no disruption to the Yang (positive energy). Sleep early and rise late, and wait for sunlight, allowing your will to be quiet and concealed, as if having private intentions or already possessing something. Avoid cold and seek warmth, preserving the skin from leakage, ensuring the energy does not escape suddenly. This is the proper response to winter energy, the way of nourishment and storage. To go against this will injure the kidneys, leading to atrophy and coldness in spring, making it hard for those who give life (i.e., caregivers) to have vitality.

    [Note: All things are collected and closed during winter; the Yang energy is stored, so do not disturb it by leaking out. Sleep early and rise late, following the nurturing and storing energy, and be sure to wait for sunlight to avoid cold evils. Keep your thoughts inward, without external distractions. If there are private intentions or if one feels content, the spirit and energy are kept within. Avoid cold and seek warmth to nurture the Yang; do not allow the skin's warmth to be leaked and its root energy to be suddenly taken away. All these are in accordance with winter energy and represent the way to nurture and store energy. To go against winter’s storing energy will injure the kidneys, leading to illness such as atrophy in spring and difficulties for caregivers.][1p]
    Discussion on Shen

    The Yellow Emperor asked: What causes cold and heat to lead to Shen? Qi Bo replied: When Yang qi declines below, it results in cold Shen; when Yin qi declines below, it results in heat Shen.

    (Note: When qi is reversed, it causes confusion, leading to dizziness or fainting, and one may suddenly lose awareness of others. This condition is termed Shen, which differs from a stroke. There are conditions of both cold and heat, and both Yin and Yang energy are involved. Both Yin and Yang qi rise from below; hence, the causes of cold and heat Shen arise from the decline of these energies below.)

    The Emperor said: The heat of heat Shen certainly arises from below the feet, why is that? Qi Bo replied: Yang qi rises from the tips of the toes, while the Yin vessels gather below the feet and converge at the soles. Therefore, when Yang qi prevails, it generates heat below the feet.

    (Note: When Yang qi dominates, Yin qi becomes deficient and Yang takes precedence, thus heat Shen originates from below the feet.)

    The Emperor said: The cold of cold Shen certainly must ascend from the toes to the knees, why is that? Qi Bo replied: Yin qi rises from within the toes, gathers beneath the knees, and converges above the knees; hence, when Yin qi prevails, it results in cold rising from the toes to the knees. This cold is not from the outside, but entirely from within.[2p]
    The note explains that the blood and energy of the Three Yin originate at the ends of the inner sides of the five fingers and gather below the knees, where the three Yin intersect above the ankles; when accumulated above the knees, the Three Yin meridians rise along the inner thigh. Thus, the cold comes not from the outside but rather from within.

    The Emperor asked: "What causes cold and convulsions?" Qi Bo replied: "The front Yin is where the Zong muscles converge, a meeting of the Tai Yin and Yang Ming. In spring and summer, Yang energy is abundant while Yin energy is sparse; in autumn and winter, Yin energy is strong while Yang energy declines. If a person is robust yet suffers from a loss during autumn and winter, their lower energy contends with the upper, failing to recover. Vital essence overflows downward, and evils rise with it. When the energy originates within, Yang energy weakens, failing to nourish the channels of the meridians. With diminishing Yang energy and only Yin remaining, the hands and feet become cold."

    The note further elaborates that the root of the Zong muscles arises from within the womb, connecting inwardly to the kidneys. The dual energies of Yin and Yang are generated in the stomach and transmitted to the Tai Yin, stored in the kidneys. The gathering of Tai Yin and Yang Ming in the Zong muscles occurs between the middle and lower Jiao, combining in the region of the front Yin. During autumn and winter, when Yang energy is conserved and Yin energy is prominent, this condition leads to cold convulsions; the robust physical nature leads one to overexert, causing lower energy to contend with upper energy, thus failing to be contained below. When Yang energy escapes upward, the essence of the Yin organs likewise overflows downward.[3p]
    Evil qi refers to the cold and dampness associated with the yin organs. The yang qi resides in the yin organs, and when the essence of yang emerges, the yin coldness rises along with it. Therefore, the yang produced in the middle burner also diminishes, unable to nourish the channels and collaterals. The qi in the upper and lower parts cannot mutually support one another, causing the yang qi to gradually deplete while the yin qi remains alone, hence the hands and feet become cold.

    The Emperor asked: "What about heat stroke, how does that occur?" Qi Bo replied: "When alcohol enters the stomach, the collaterals become full while the main channels are empty. The spleen is responsible for transporting the fluids of the stomach. When yin qi is deficient, yang qi intrudes; when yang qi intrudes, the stomach becomes unharmonious. If the stomach is unharmonious, the essence and qi are depleted; if the essence and qi are depleted, it cannot nourish the four limbs. This person must frequently get drunk, especially after indulging, as the qi accumulates in the spleen and cannot disperse. The qi of the alcohol mingles with the qi of the grains, creating excessive internal heat, which spreads throughout the body, leading to internal heat and red urine. The abundant alcohol qi is fierce, which gradually diminishes the kidney qi, allowing the yang qi to dominate, hence the hands and feet become hot.

    Note: Wei qi is the vigorous qi of water and grains. Alcohol is also a vigorous and hot liquid derived from water and grains, therefore it follows the wei qi to surface on the skin and fills the collaterals, rather than moving through the channels alongside the spleen qi, resulting in full collaterals and empty channels. If it does not pass through the spleen qi to circulate in the channels, then yin qi is deficient.[4p]
    When the fierce heat rises from outside to within, the Yang energy enters. The Yangming is the organ of dryness and heat, which derives its essence from the Yin of the Taiyin. When the Yin energy is deficient and Yang heat enters, the stomach energy becomes unbalanced, leading to a depletion of the vital essences that cannot nourish the limbs. If one drinks alcohol excessively, the alcohol energy accumulates in the spleen; if one indulges excessively, the food energy remains trapped in the stomach, and the spleen cannot metabolize its essences. As the food energy accumulates and cannot disperse, the alcohol energy and food energy invade each other, resulting in excessive internal heat. The heat from the central region spreads to the surroundings, causing heat to pervade the body. If the food and drink entering the stomach cannot circulate the vital essences downward to the bladder, this results in internal heat and red urine. The kidneys, as the water organs, receive and store the essences of food and water. When the alcohol heat is strong and vigorous, the vital essences of the kidneys diminish daily, the Yin energy dwindles below, and the Yang energy prevails within, causing the hands and feet to become hot.

    The Emperor then asked: Why do some experience abdominal fullness, some suddenly become unaware of their surroundings, and some may take half a day or even a whole day to regain awareness? Qibo replied: When Yin energy is strong above, the lower part becomes deficient, leading to abdominal fullness. When Yang energy is strong above, it causes the lower energy to press upwards, creating a reversal of evil energies. This reversal disrupts the Yang energy, and when the Yang energy is disordered, it results in a loss of awareness.[5p]
    Note: When the yang is obstructed from knowing the person, there may suddenly arise confusion or fainting. The qi of half a day refers to the half cycle of qi circulation, while the qi of a whole day refers to the complete cycle of qi. When the yin qi is strong above, it indicates damage to the yang qi in the middle burner, with the yin qi alone prevailing above. When the yin is dominant above, the yang qi of the lower burner is also deficient, leading to yang deficiency below, which causes abdominal distension. The lower qi refers to the primordial yang of the lower burner, and the evil qi is the cold water of the kidneys. When the yang qi is strong above, it signifies that the yin qi is deficient and the yang qi prevails alone. When the yang is strong above, the lower qi rises up; if the lower qi ascends, cold evil follows and rises against it, disrupting the yang qi above and causing sudden confusion.

    The Emperor said: Good. I wish to hear about the conditions of the six meridians and the diseases they represent. Qibo replied: If there is blockage in the Greater Yang, the head becomes swollen and heavy, and the feet cannot move, leading to fainting or collapsing.

    Note: If the yang of the feet is reversed upwards, it causes swelling in the head and head pain; if it reverses downwards, then the feet cannot move, both being diseases of the Greater Yang. When the spirit and qi become confused, it leads to dizziness and fainting, as the Greater Yang is the master of all yang energies.

    If the yangming is blocked, it results in manic agitation, a desire to run and shout, abdominal fullness that prevents lying down, a red and hot face, and delusions of seeing and speaking falsely.

    Note: Mania, agitation, shouting, and delusional speech and sight are diseases of the yangming meridian.[6p]
    Due to the reversal of qi, the abdomen is bloated, and if the stomach is not harmonious, one cannot sleep. The Yangming channel is the channel of dryness and heat; its qi emerges at the face, hence the face is red and hot. If the Shaoyang channel is in a state of reversal, there will be sudden deafness, swelling and heat in the cheeks, pain in the flanks, and the legs will be unable to move.

    In the case of the Taiyin channel's reversal, there is abdominal fullness and swelling, difficulty with bowel movements, lack of appetite, and if one eats, there will be vomiting, preventing sleep. This is because, when food and drink enter the stomach, the spleen is responsible for transformation and transportation; if qi is reversed in the spleen, there will be difficulty with bowel movements. If the spleen does not transport and regulate, then the stomach will also not be harmonious, resulting in vomiting and inability to sleep.

    In the event of the Shaoyin channel's reversal, there may be dry mouth, red urine, abdominal fullness, and heart pain. This occurs because the reversal of the meridian prevents the yin fluids from ascending, leading to dry mouth and heart pain. The lung channel cannot regulate smoothly downward, hence the red urine. The interaction of water and fire, yin and yang qi does not harmonize, resulting in abdominal fullness.

    For the Jueyin channel's reversal, there will be swelling and pain in the lower abdomen, abdominal distention, difficulty with urination, a tendency to sleep while bending the knees, swelling of the yin areas, and internal heat in the legs. The reversal causes swelling and pain in the lower abdomen and abdominal bloating, with difficulty in urination and swelling in the yin areas.[7p]
    The liver governs the tendons, and the knee is where the tendons converge. When the meridians experience counterflow, they cannot nourish the tendons and bones, thus leading to a tendency to lie down with the knees bent. The Jueyin wood and fire govern qi, causing counterflow and resulting in swelling and heat in the knee.

    When there is excess, it should be drained; when there is deficiency, it should be replenished. When there is neither excess nor deficiency, it should be adjusted according to the meridian.

    Note: Since the counterflow occurs in the meridians, treatment should follow the meridian. If the qi in the meridian is excessive, use needles to drain and disperse it. If the qi is deficient, use needles to tonify it. When there is neither excess nor deficiency, harmonizing movements of the primary meridian is termed 'meridian needling.'

    In the case of Taiyin counterflow, when the knee is cramping sharply, and there is pain in the heart radiating to the abdomen, it treats the main disease.

    Note: The qi of the Central Plains governs the nourishment of surrounding areas. When the Foot Taiyin qi is in counterflow, it causes cramping in the knee. The spleen qi is counterflowing and cannot transport its essence, which leads to heart qi being deficient and causing pain radiating to the abdomen. This is a disease originating from the spleen, so it is necessary to treat the spleen qi directly.

    In the case of Shaoyin counterflow, with fullness and vomiting, causing clear diarrhea, it treats the main disease.

    Note: The qi of Shaoyin combines with Yangming from above to govern the transformation of food and fluids. The counterflow of Shaoyin qi leads to excessive fullness in the middle burner, resulting in vomiting. When the qi of water and fire does not transform properly, it results in clear, cold diarrhea.[8p]
    The cold and reverse flow of the liver causes pain in the waist, fullness in the front, delirium, and treats the principal diseases. Note: "Contraction" is governed by the liver, the waist is the exterior of the liver, "fullness" means that food and qi cannot disperse the essence in the liver, and "front closure" indicates the liver governs smooth flow. The liver governs speech; delirium occurs when liver qi is stagnant.

    When all three yin are reversed, movement in the front and back ceases, causing coldness in the hands and feet, leading to death in three days. Note: "All three yin are reversed" indicates a separation of yin and yang. When there is no movement in the front and back, the yin pertains to the lower body. Since all yang energy is born from yin, if all three yin are reversed, the life force is extinguished, resulting in cold hands and feet and death in three days.

    The taiyang reverse flow causes stiffness, collapse, vomiting blood, and nosebleeds, treating the principal diseases. Note: The reverse flow of taiyang energy causes stiffness and collapse. When yang energy rises excessively, it causes vomiting of blood, and when yang heat is in the upper body, it causes nosebleeds.

    The shaoyang reverse flow leads to dysfunction in the joints. When the joints are dysfunctional, the waist cannot move, and the neck cannot turn. Note: Shaoyang governs the joints; therefore, if shaoyang energy is in reverse, the joints are affected. The neck and nape signify the convergence of the three yang, and the waist and spine are significant joints in the body; thus, if the joints are dysfunctional, the waist cannot turn, and the neck cannot turn.

    If there is an abscess in the intestines, it cannot be treated; death will occur if there is shock.[9p]
    【Note: The Lesser Yang fire governs Qi; when fire reverses internally, it leads to intestinal abscesses. Intestinal abscesses that cannot be treated indicate that the disease is within the Qi level and the abscess is internal, beyond the possibility of needling. If there is a shock, the toxic Qi invades the organs, thus leading to death.】 The Greater Yang presents with counterflow Qi, wheezing, cough, body heat, and tendency to bleed from the nose and vomit blood. 【Note: When Greater Yang Qi is counterflowing, it causes wheezing; when reversing, it leads to coughing. Greater Yang governs the muscles, so when it is counterflowing, the body feels warm. Greater Yang is essentially a fiercely hot Qi; when Qi reverses, it forces blood to move erratically, thus causing vomiting of blood.】 The Hand Taiyin exhibits counterflow with fullness and cough, prone to spitting up foam, leading to treatment of the main disease. 【Note: The Hand Taiyin lung governs Qi; when it reverses, it leads to fullness and cough; not able to freely distribute body fluids, it leads to spitting up foam. This refers to diseases originating from the lung, thus treating the lung Qi of the main illness.】 The Hand Shenyin presents with counterflow leading to heart pain radiating to the throat, body heat, and death that cannot be treated.[10p]
    The hands represent the qi of the heart's pericardium and the heart itself. The pericardium acts as the sovereign fire, and when the two fires oppose each other, they will consume themselves, leading to an incurable death.

    When there is a reversal in the hand's solar yang, it results in deafness, tears, inability to turn the neck, and the waist cannot bend up or down. These conditions are linked to the illness.

    If an illness arises from the hand's solar yang, it causes deafness. The small intestine governs fluids; if it reverses, it causes tears that fail to nourish the meridians, hence the neck cannot be turned, and the waist cannot bend. The waist and neck are significant junctions of the meridian system.

    When there is a reversal in the hand's yangming and shaoyang, it results in throat phlegm, swelling, and paralysis of the throat, indicating the illness.

    The hand's yangming corresponds to the lungs, while the hand's shaoyang relates to the pericardium and the sanjiao. The yangming governs the throat, and the lungs govern the voice; when the fire of the sanjiao is also in opposition, it causes throat phlegm and swelling. The yangming is a dry and hot channel, and the sanjiao is associated with the fire of thunder; when both heat and fire are in opposition, it leads to paralysis.[11p]
    The Emperor said: If a person has a headache that persists for several years, how can this be explained? What is the name of this illness? Qi Bo replied: It is likely due to an exposure to extreme cold that has penetrated to the marrow. The marrow is governed by the brain. When the brain is affected, it causes headaches and also tooth pain; this illness is called "Jue Ni." The Emperor said: Excellent!

    Section on Major Anomalies

    The two Yin conditions urgently cause seizures. The two Yin refers to the Lesser Yin. A seizure is characterized by fainting, collapsing, and being unaware of one’s surroundings. This is because the watery Qi is surging upon the heart, leading to an urgent pulse in the two Yin channels. When the pulse feels like panting, it is called "Bao Jue." Bao Jue refers to one being unable to communicate with others during a fainting spell. This urgent and slippery pulse indicates phlegm and water obstructing, hence it feels urgent and slippery, referred to as Bao Jue.

    Section on Pulse Analysis

    The condition referred to as "entering the center" and becoming mute indicates that the Yang has become abundant and then declined, resulting in muteness. If the inner energy is depleted and leads to Jue, this indicates kidney deficiency. If the Lesser Yin does not arrive, it indicates Jue. "Entering the center and becoming mute" means the Yang has become abundant and then declined, resulting in a deficiency of the vital energy, leading to muteness. When Yang is abundant externally but its stored energy is depleted, it results in kidney deficiency. If Yang receives energy from the limbs but then declines, the extremities do not retract, resulting in lethargy. If the kidney energy is insufficient, it leads to muteness, preventing the Qi of the Lesser Yin from arriving, causing coldness in the hands and feet.[12p]
    On Regulating Menstruation

    When there is excess ambition, it leads to abdominal distension and diarrhea; when there is insufficiency, it results in cold extremities.

    [Note: The kidneys are the gate of the stomach; if they are not functioning properly, water accumulates and causes abdominal distension and diarrhea. The kidneys are the origin of vital energy, thus insufficiency leads to coldness and counterflow.]

    The collateral vessels and sun vessels both connect to the meridians; when blood and qi are combined, it results in fullness. When blood and qi ascend together, it leads to great reversal, causing sudden death. If qi reverses back, there is life; if it does not reverse, there is death.

    [Note: The blood and qi of the collateral vessels and sun vessels both connect to the meridians, thus blood and qi together are substantial. When blood and qi ascend together, it results in great counterflow, which can lead to sudden death. If qi reverses back, there is life; if it does not, there is death.]

    On Vital Energy Connecting to Heaven

    Yang energy, when overworked, expands and depletes, leading to accumulation in summer, resulting in heat exhaustion.

    [Note: Overwork damages yang energy; in summer, yang energy rises exteriorly, thus increasing deficiency and causing heat exhaustion.]

    Great anger causes the physical energy to be severed and blood to accumulate above, leading to lightheadedness.

    [Note: Anger raises qi, causing blood to flow with it; when qi and blood reverse, it leads to impending faintness.][13p]

    Discussion on Yin and Yang

    The Three Yangs result in illness manifesting as cold and heat, leading to boils and swellings, as well as atrophy and numbness.

    Note: The Three Yangs refer to the Taiyang, which governs the exterior. When an evil force penetrates, it starts at the skin and hair, clashing with the righteous qi, resulting in illnesses characterized by cold and heat. Taiyang governs opening; if illness prevents this, the evil qi obstructs the flesh, leading to boils and swellings. Taiyang is the master of all Yang qi and governs the tendons; if the tendons are harmed, it results in atrophy; if the qi is harmed, it leads to numbness.

    Treatise on Pulse and Its Subtleties

    Numbness leads to vertigo.

    Note: Numbness is the reversal of qi upwards. When qi solely reverses upwards, it transforms into a condition of the head.

    Comprehensive Evaluation of Deficiency and Excess

    Jaundice, acute pain, epilepsy, and convulsive states are born from prolonged reversals.

    Note: Jaundice is due to damp heat accumulating internally, with the resulting discoloration appearing externally. Acute pain arises from an imbalance of qi within the five organs, resulting in sudden pain. Vertigo and convulsions are due to excess or deficiency of Yin and Yang manifesting as illness. All of these arise from prolonged disharmony of the Yin-Yang and the Five Elements.

    Commentary on the Yangming Pulse

    In Yangming deficiency, there is wheezing and lamentation; lamentation indicates aversion to people.[14p]
    The Emperor asked: When there is a disease causing fever and sweating, yet the feeling of fullness and restlessness does not resolve with sweating, what is this illness? Qi Bo replied: Sweating and fever indicate wind, but when sweating does not relieve the feeling of fullness and restlessness, it is due to obstruction (jue). This illness is called wind obstruction.

    The note explains: Wind is a yang pathogen that opens the skin and causes fluids to leak out; when wind-heat remains, it leads to fever. If wind-heat does not dispel, it can harm the kidney energy and cause it to reverse upward. When it reverses upwards, it induces heart restlessness; when it affects the spleen, it causes a feeling of fullness. The sickness is named wind obstruction because it arises from the wind pathogen causing the kidney energy to reverse.

    The Emperor requested to hear more. Qi Bo continued: The great yang governs energy, so it is the first to receive pathogens. The lesser yin is its internal counterpart. If heat is present, it follows that the energy will become obstructed. The Emperor asked: How should it be treated? Qi Bo replied: Treat both the exterior and interior by needling, and administer medicinal soup.

    The note elaborates: The energy of the greater yang governs the exterior, while wind is a yang pathogen that injures human yang energy; the clash of two yangs results in heat illness. The lesser yin and greater yang correspond internally and externally; when yang heat is on the surface, the yin energy follows, resulting in obstruction. Needle the exterior to dispel the yang pathogen of wind-heat, and needle the interior to address the reversed energy of the lesser yin; give medicinal soup to assist with the fluid and sweat.[15p]
    Discussion on Needling

    When the evil influences are at the networks of the Foot Shaoyin, Taiyin, and Foot Yangming, all five networks converge at the ear. If these five networks are exhausted, all the arteries in the body begin to move, yet the body remains unaware, resembling a corpse, sometimes referred to as corpse syndrome. If one has cut the hair at the left ear by an inch and burns it, then drinks a cup of fine wine. If one cannot drink, pour it down their throat immediately.

    [Note: All meridians originate in the Foot Shaoyin kidneys, are produced in the Foot Yangming stomach, conveyed through the Foot Taiyin spleen, governed by the Hand Shaoyin heart, and directed to the Hand Taiyin lungs; thus, the energy of the five meridians converges at the ear. The network at the left ear is linked to the liver, which rules blood and resides on the left, its energy rising to the crown. When all five networks are exhausted, the nourishment and defense do not circulate, causing the body’s arteries to tremble yet remain unaware, termed corpse syndrome. The reason one lives and moves is through the circulation of energy and blood; when blood and energy do not flow, the form becomes like a corpse. Needle the great toe at the hidden white point of the Foot Taiyin, needle the heart at the springing point of the Foot Shaoyin; needle the middle finger at the mouth of the Foot Yangming; needle the great finger at the lesser merchant point of the Hand Taiyin; needle the heart's master point of the Hand Shaoyin. This will clear the blood and energy, and the syndrome will cease. If it does not cease, use a bamboo tube to blow at both ears to clear the ancestral vessels, cut the hair at the left ear to clear the nourishing blood, and drink fine wine to clear the defensive energy.][16p]
    On the Great Discussion of the Changes of Qi

    In years when water is excessive, cold qi flows, disturbing the heart fire and causing the people to suffer from yin collapse.

    On the Great Discussion of the Five Constants

    When metal is insufficient, it is termed as following the changes. The period of transformation is called "breaking and receiving." Its qi rises, its use is hasty and sharp, and its movement is like a clang that confuses and collapses.

    When the lesser yang is in control of heaven, there is qi reversal.

    The earth is in the center; if the diaphragm is not open, then there is a reversal of qi between above and below. When the greater yin is in control of heaven, the damp qi descends, and the kidney qi rises, causing a reversal of qi.

    If the yang qi does not rise, then the hands and feet will experience qi reversal.

    On the Great Discussion of the Correct Principles of the Six Origins

    When water is stagnant, the people tend to experience qi reversal.

    The reversal of qi arises from the storage of yang qi below, which causes a blockage in the middle qi.

    On the Great Discussion of the Most True Essentials

    When the yang brightness is at the spring, if it dominates excessively, there will be cold collapse in the intestines, surging upward to the chest, leading to severe breathlessness and an inability to stand for long.

    The cold collapse in the intestines surges up to the chest, causing breathlessness, as the cold qi ascends against the yang brightness of the large intestine, reaching the lungs in the chest. When the sun prevails, if cold collapse enters the stomach, it leads to internal heart pain.[17p]
    The one who reverses and enters the stomach, water insults the earth. The stomach channels connect upwards to the heart, hence the heartache. The return of the sun causes the counterflow of qi to rise.

    This refers to the stagnant cold qi rising, which resembles the qi from a year and a half prior. All counterflows downward belong to the lower regions. When the yang qi above reverses, it causes counter-cold. The lesser yin is in the spring, ruling that when victorious, the counter qi rises causing heart pain.

    The ascending counter qi is governed by cold water, which ascends above the ruler fire in spring.

    Regarding the discussion on abundance and decline, the thunder god asked how to distinguish the amount of qi and which is contrary and which is following. The Yellow Emperor replied: yang moves from the left, yin from the right. The elderly move from above, the young from below. Thus, spring and summer returning to yang signifies life, while returning to autumn and winter signifies death. Conversely, returning to autumn and winter can signify life, hence the excessive qi that is contrary is all a counterflow.

    The question arose: Is an excess considered a counterflow? The answer was: If rising without descending, then cold counterflow reaches the knees, leading to death in the young during autumn and winter while the elderly may live. When qi rises without descending, headaches occur and the crown of the head experiences illness. Seeking yang yields nothing, while seeking yin is unclear; the five regions are isolated without signs, akin to being in a wilderness or lying in an empty chamber, endlessly incomplete within the day. Therefore, the lesser qi’s counterflow leads to delusive dreams, reaching the ultimate state of confusion.

    The comment on yang moving from the left indicates that the qi of spring and summer flows from the left to the right, and the yin from the right indicates that the qi of autumn and winter flows from the right to the left.[18p]
    The energy of the elderly descends from above, like the autumn atmosphere gradually declining downwards; the energy of the young ascends from below, like the spring atmosphere flourishing upwards. Therefore, the energies of spring and summer return to the Yang, moving from left to right, which follows the natural order, hence this is the vitality; while the energies of autumn and winter return to the Yin, moving from right to left, which defies the order, thus this is the state of decline. Conversely, the autumn and winter energies returning to the Yin moving from right to left signify life, while returning to spring and summer moving from left to right signifies disorder. Thus, regardless of the amount of energy, anything contrary signifies stagnation.

    One speaks of a single Yin energy. If it rises and does not descend, and the cold stagnation reaches the knees, this is the ascending of Yin energy according to the dictates of autumn and winter. Therefore, the elderly align with the natural order, while the young are contrary. The energy discussed here pertains to a single Yang energy. If it rises and does not descend, and headaches manifest, this represents Yang energy ascending directly to the crown.

    If one is unaware of the way the heavens, earth, and humanity combine, seeking Yang without attaining the energy, or seeking Yin without discerning its subtleties, then one becomes cut off and lacks evidence. A deficiency in energy leads to the reversed ascension of energy.[19p]
    Discussion on Subtle Essence

    When the energies converge, the eyes are unable to see. In a person, the yang energy gathers above, and the yin energy gathers below. When yang gathers above, fire shines alone; when yin gathers below, the feet become cold, and cold feet lead to swelling. Water cannot withstand five fires, hence the eyes become blind.

    [Note: The essence of the kidneys does not ascend and connect with the eyes, hence there is no vision. "Convergence" refers to the gathering of various yang energies above and various yin energies below. The heart is the sun among the yang, specializing in the five organs' essence; thus, when yang gathers above without the harmonization of yin energy, fire shines alone above. The kidneys are the organ of water, storing the essence of the five organs, and the yin veins gather at the feet and concentrate at the soles. When yin gathers below without the harmonization of yang energy, the feet become cold, leading to cold organs and fullness diseases. The term "water" refers to the water of the sun, while "five fires" refers to the yang energies of the five organs. Therefore, when yin and yang are reversed, the eyes become blind. "Blind" refers to the two bright eyes of the sun, aligned with the heavens' sun and moon.][20p]
    Classic Text on the Spirit Pivot:

    On the Manifestations of Pathogenic Qi in the Organs

    When the heart pulse is weak and sluggish, it results in cessation of the limbs.
    Note: "Cessation" refers to the four limbs. The heart is the solar energy among the Yang organs, hence the hands and feet become cold.

    When the kidney pulse is weak and rapid, it results in fainting or sudden anxiety.
    Note: The kidneys are the source of vital energy; when the upright qi is deficient and cold, it leads to fainting. The deficiency of qi reacting inversely causes sudden anxiety.

    On the Original Spirit

    When kidney qi is deficient, it leads to cessation.
    Note: The kidneys are the source of vital energy, therefore deficiency leads to cessation.

    On the Meridians

    The pulse of the Lung's Hand Taiyin is characterized by severe movement leading to dizziness when the two hands cross, which indicates limb cessation. This pulse governs lung-related illnesses, causing pain and cessation in the inner and anterior areas of the upper arm.
    Note: Dizziness due to crossing the hands is caused by kidney qi rebounding. The pain and cessation in the upper arm represents the affected section of the meridian.

    The pulse of the Heart's Hand Shaoyin, when in motion, causes dryness in the throat, heart pain, thirst, and the desire to drink, which indicates limb cessation; this pulse governs heart-related illnesses, resulting in pain and cessation in the inner and posterior areas of the upper arm.
    Note: The upper arm is the section governed by the central pulse.

    The pulse of the Bladder's Foot Taiyang, when in movement, leads to headaches, bulging eyes, a stiff neck, back pain, waist discomfort, difficulty bending the hip, tightness in the knee, and sensation of rupture in the ankle, indicating ankle cessation.
    Note: This illness pertains to the energy of the Taiyang.[21p]
    The pulse of the Kidney's Lesser Yin, when in motion, results in the illness of hunger with no desire for food, and the face appears like lacquered wood. When coughing and expectorating, there is blood; wheezing and gasping occur, sitting but wanting to rise, eyes cannot see anything, and the heart feels suspended as if in hunger. If the qi is insufficient, there is great fear; the heart feels restless as if one is about to be captured, which is termed bone deficiency. This indicates diseases originating from the Kidney, such as weakness and deficiency.

    (Note: Above the Lesser Yin, the Ruler Fire governs. When the Lesser Yin is in motion, the qi of up and down does not communicate, hence the lack of desire for food and the heart feeling suspended as if in hunger. If qi is insufficient below, there will be great fear; if insufficient above, the heart feels restless as if one is about to be captured. The Lesser Yin belongs to the Kidney, which is linked above to the Lung, and the Kidney is the source of vital qi. When the face appears like lacquered wood, it indicates that the qi of the Lesser Yin does not rise. Coughing with blood and wheezing indicates that the vital qi of the Lesser Yin does not ascend and is instead rebellious in the Lung.)[22p]
    To sit and desire to rise is a sign of agitation, indicating that the energy of the Lesser Yin is stagnant below and wishes to ascend. The essence of the bones is related to vision; if the eyes see nothing, it is because the essence does not rise. This represents the vital energy of the Lesser Yin kidneys that is obstructed below, resulting in various ailments, hence it is termed bone obstruction.

    The gallbladder's channel, associated with the Greater Yang, manifests as bitterness in the mouth when it is agitated, along with sighing, pain in the chest and flanks, an inability to turn over, and in severe cases, a fine dust appears on the face, while the body lacks moisture, and there is external heat in the feet, which is termed Yang obstruction.

    Note: When agitated, it causes bitterness in the mouth, frequent sighing, chest and flank pain, and an inability to turn over, indicating that the energy of the Greater Yang does not rise. The Greater Yang governs the initial energy of life, thus the gallbladder energy rises, and the energies of the eleven organs also ascend. When the energy of the Greater Yang moves abnormally, it obstructs and does not ascend, leading to symptoms such as fine dust on the face and a lack of moisture in the body. The fire energy of the Greater Yang governs the breath; when the feet are hot, it indicates fire is obstructed below, resulting from the reverse of Yang energy.[23p]
    Five Disorders

    Clear qi resides in yin, while turbid qi is in yang. Nourishing qi flows smoothly through the channels, while defending qi moves against the current. When clear and turbid qi interfere, it causes chaos in the chest, which is known as great confusion. Therefore, when qi is in disorder in the limbs, it results in the four extremities being cold; when it is chaotic in the head, it leads to reversed flow, causing heaviness and dizziness in the head.

    Reversal and Order of Weight

    The Yellow Emperor asked: Why does the lesser yin pulse flow downward alone? Qi Bo replied: The chong vessel is the sea of the five viscera and six bowels; all are nourished by it. The upper part emerges from the temples, permeates the yang, and irrigates the essence; the lower part enters the great network of the lesser yin, emerging from the qi street, flowing along the inner thigh into the knee, lying within the skin of the calf, and descending to the back of the inner ankle. The lower section connects with the lesser yin channel and penetrates the three yin; the front part flows within the foot, descending along the ankle, entering between the big toe, nourishing the network and warming the muscles. Thus, when the network is obstructed, the ankle remains immobile; if it does not move, it results in cold extremities, which leads to disorder.[24p]
    If one is timid and frail, then the pathways of water will not be effective, and the energy will dissipate. The energy of the five organs and six bowels is all derived from the Chong channel. Those that rise from the head diffuse through the Yang and flow into the Yin; those that descend are connected to the Lesser Yin's major channel, exiting at the Qi Street. The blood and energy of the five organs and six bowels all pass through the Chong channel and permeate between the skin and meridians, responding to water and following Qi to operate on the surface. The Lesser Yin governs the primal water and fire, which are essence and energy. The Chong channel and the meridian of Lesser Yin permeate the three Yin channels, circulating through the ankles and entering between the big toes, radiating through the collaterals to warm the muscles. This essence and energy of the Lesser Yin flows out and operates beyond the channels and skin. Therefore, if the collaterals are obstructed, the energy of the Lesser Yin cannot circulate through the ankle, causing the ankle to become immobile. When it is immobile, it indicates that the energy of the Lesser Yin is stagnant within, leading to coldness.

    The Thunder Lord said: Young ones, those who hear the wind are at the beginning of myriad illnesses; reversal indicates the onset of cold dampness. How does one differentiate? The Yellow Emperor replied: The regular phenomenon is that at the gate of the palace, thin moisture produces wind, turbid energy causes obstruction in the body, and on the ground it leads to reversal; these are the norms, each indicated by its corresponding color concerning the disease.

    (Note: "Ground" refers to the Earth Pavilion. Wind represents the weather, thus regularly appearing at the palace courtyard. Cold dampness indicates the energy of the Earth, hence it is observed in the terrestrial area. Wind is a Yang pathology, hence its color is thin moisture. Cold dampness is a Yin pathology, hence its color is turbid energy.)[25p]

    Treatise on Qi of the Wei

    If the lower regions are empty, then [the issue arises].

    [Note: The lower regions being empty refers to emptiness at the root.]

    Treatise on the Beginning of Various Illnesses

    The onset of accumulation begins; it manifests with the cold, and thus it leads to accumulation. [Note: The onset of accumulation begins as a result of cold. The clear dampness evils reverse downward and result in accumulation.] When the qi of accumulation arises in the feet, it causes cold to arise in the shins; when the shins are cold, then the blood vessels become stagnant. [Note: If evil qi reverses downward, it causes congestion in the shins, preventing smooth flow. This leads to cold, and with cold, the blood vessels become stagnant.]

    Treatise on Needling Specific Points for True Evils

    When the qi is in the feet, the ancestral qi does not descend, and the blood in the vessels coagulates and stops; without fire to regulate it, it cannot be retrieved. [Note: The qi in the feet refers to the repletion of the Lesser Yin qi. Cold qi reverses downward, which prevents the ancestral qi from descending, causing the blood to coagulate and stop. Without fire to regulate it, it cannot be transmitted; this refers to the essence qi of the lower regions, where the interplay of yin and yang, water and fire, requires heat to warm the cold water.][26p]
    Bian Que’s Classic of Difficult Issues

    Reversal of Qi

    If the illness is accompanied by delirium or nonsensical speech, there should be heat in the body, the pulse should be rapid and large; however, if the hands and feet are cold and the pulse is deep, thin, and weak, it indicates death.

    Essentials from the Golden Chamber (Han, Zhang Ji)

    Reversal of Qi

    In the section on internal organs, it is stated: A question is posed: When the pulse is deep, large, and slippery, the deepness indicates something real, while the slipperiness indicates Qi. When the real Qi clashes, it causes blood Qi to enter the internal organs, leading to death; if it enters the bowels, recovery occurs. This is known as sudden reversal. What does this mean? The teacher says: The lips and mouth may be blue, and the body cold, indicating entry into the internal organs, leading to death; if the body is warm and there is spontaneous sweating, it indicates entry into the bowels, leading to recovery.

    In the section on abdominal fullness: If there is abdominal pain with a tight, wiry pulse, the tightness indicates stagnation of defensive Qi, leading to aversion to cold; the wiriness indicates lack of appetite; when evil and correct Qi clash, it results in cold hernia. Cold hernia causes pain around the navel, and if it develops, a white fluid may be discharged, with hands and feet feeling cold; if the pulse is deep and tight, the decoction of Aconitum should be employed.

    In the section on water Qi: If the pulse at the wrist is slow and thin, the slowness indicates coldness, while thinness indicates insufficient blood. The pulse at the foot yin position is weak and slow; weakness indicates Qi, slowness indicates cold, and insufficient cold Qi results in hands and feet feeling cold. If hands and feet are cold, the nourishing and guarding Qi is disturbed, leading to abdominal fullness and sounds in the sides that chase each other. When Qi reaches the bladder, both the nourishing and guarding Qi are exhausted.[27p]
    When the Yang energy is blocked, the body becomes cold; when the Yin energy is blocked, there is pain in the bones. When Yang energy flows first, there is aversion to cold; when Yin energy flows first, there is numbness and paralysis. When Yin and Yang complement each other, their energies circulate. When the vital energy changes, it disperses. If it is full, energy is lost; if it is deficient, there is incontinence, termed the energy division.

    In the Vomiting chapter: for dry vomiting and retching, or when hands and feet are cold, the tangerine peel decoction is the main treatment.

    In the Diarrhea chapter: when the Qi of the six bowels is blocked externally, the hands and feet become cold, the upper body qi is tight, and the feet shrink; when the Qi of the five organs is blocked internally, diarrhea occurs without restraint, and in severe cases, the hands and feet become numb.

    For diarrhea with cold hands and feet and no pulse, if moxibustion is applied and it does not warm, and the pulse does not return, accompanied by slight wheezing, it indicates death. The lesser Yin's resistance to the Yang is considered proper.

    For diarrhea with clear fluids, there must be accompanied sweating and resolution; the patient must exhibit slight syncope, because their face is warm, indicating a deficiency below.

    For diarrhea accompanied by a cessation of the pulse, cold hands and feet, if the pulse returns at a later stage and the hands and feet are warm, there is life; if the pulse does not return, it indicates death.[28p]
    On Yang Illness

    Sudden winds and scorching heat, clouds and objects flying about, morning darkness to evening brightness, hot nights and cold days, responding to cold yet not cold, expecting rain yet no rain, water dried up and soil damaged, years of great drought, grass and trees withering, rivers running dry—this is the Yang illness of heaven and earth.

    Violent blockages, sudden shortness of breath, limbs unable to move, the two bowels not functioning, deafness and blindness, dry throat and scorched mouth, sores on the throat and tongue, clear nasal discharge, flushed cheeks and restless heart, dizziness and heavy head, eyes like fire, whole body feeling burned, those who usually cannot suddenly able, those who usually do not want suddenly wanting, climbing high to sing and laugh, shedding clothes and running, speaking wildly and irrationally, unable to distinguish kin from stranger, doing things heedlessly, drinking water without rest, chest bloated, abdomen and sides full and uncomfortable, back ulcers and rotting flesh, restless and collapsing inward, food not entering the stomach, water not passing through the intestines, sudden swelling and fullness, shouting and becoming muddled, losing awareness, pain without a known location—this is the Yang illness in a person.

    The pulse of Yang illness, strong when pressed, signifies life; absent signifies death.[29p]
    On Yin and Yang

    Frost flies, hail runs; dawn and dusk bring haze. Clouds and rain drift, winds and dew are cold. The heat is not hot, while the cold arrives before it is cold. The weather is damp and stagnant, springs arise in fields, mountains crumble and earth splits, soil deteriorates and rivers overflow; the moon is obscured, and the sun dims. This is the manifestation of Yin and its cessation in heaven and earth.

    When there is sudden and harsh cold, the body feels tight and constricted; the limbs are clenched, lips turn blue, face becomes dark, eyes are wide while the mouth is shut, the heart and abdomen feel fullness and pain, the head shakes and throbs, the waist and feet are heavy; speech becomes difficult, there is vomiting and diarrhea, there is numbness on both sides, bowel movements are uncontrollable, swallowing brings sourness. There is sorrow and distress; emotions fluctuate erratically — this is the manifestation of Yin and its cessation in a person.

    The pulse of Yin and its cessation: if the pulse is weak when lifting the finger and strong when pressing it, life is present; if both lifting and pressing are absent, death occurs. If the whole body is cold and sweat appears on the forehead, that too signifies death. Illness of Yin and its cessation should not be treated for more than three days.[30p]
    When yang qi ascends and does not descend, it is called "contrary." When yin qi descends and does not ascend, it is also called "contrary." When yang qi descends and does not ascend, it is called "blocked," and when yin qi ascends and does not descend, it is also called "blocked." "Contrary and blocked" refers to the inability of yin and yang to correspond with each other. When yang rushes above, it causes burning, leading to jaundice from the spleen and lungs, which manifests as a yellow-red color, arising from the extreme of yang. When yin runs below, it causes freezing, leading to cold extremities from the kidneys and liver, which presents as a green-black color, arising from the extreme of yin. Jaundice refers to yellow jaundice, and cold extremities refer to cold extremities due to the obstruction and non-communication of yin and yang. For yang's burning, treat with water; for yin's cold extremities, assist with fire; thus, it is the way of mutual support between yin and yang.

    Regarding moxibustion, if one should administer it but does not, it results in cold extremities and reverses the flow.

    For illnesses that warrant moxibustion, it opens the yin to connect with yang. Failing to perform moxibustion leads to heavy condensations of cold qi, toxic yin accumulating internally, qi of cold extremities surging upwards, creating separation and obliteration.

    Concerning fatal pulses:

    For conditions of cold extremities, if the pulse is floating, large, and short, it is fatal.
    For cold extremities, if one calls but there is no response, and the pulse is absent, it is fatal.
    For fullness in the cold extremities, if the pulse is long, it is fatal.
    For cold extremities with sweating, if the pulse is weak and slow, it is fatal.

    Pulse Classic by Wang Shuhe:

    Regarding pulse methods:

    For simultaneous deficiency of liver and gallbladder: if in the right hand at the pulse position both yin and yang are deficient, it indicates deficiency in the foot's lesser yin and lesser yang channels. The patient suffers from confusion and is unable to recognize people, has hallucinations, feels weak and cannot speak, and is often startled. The governing channel illness presents with a strong spine and cold extremities.[31p]
    When entering, it is the yang riding on the yin. The symptoms include a cool body with cold limbs and a bad hot feeling, indicating external yin and internal yang; however, if one feels neither hot nor thirsty, that means both inside and outside are yin. Zhongjing states: if the cold is deep, the heat is also deep; if the cold is mild, the heat is mild too. Mouth sores that are rotten and red come from excessive sweating.

    On Yin and Yang, Cold and Heat

    Intense yang leads to an intense yin, and an intense yin leads to an intense yang; this is the transformation of cold and heat. For instance, if the hands and feet are abnormally cold, accompanied by constipation and red urine, or black stool, with a pulse that is deep and slippery, this indicates a yang syndrome. For mild cases, use Baihu Decoction; for severe cases, use Chengqi Decoction.

    In the case of cold damage and withdrawal, if blood and qi do not circulate, causing the limbs to become abnormally cold, this implies deep hidden heat, hence a deep state of cold. In such cases, urgently use a large dose of Chengqi Decoction with a supplementary laxative; immediate sweating will result. This aligns with Zhongjing's assertion that a cold state should be dealt with using laxatives.

    Heat-induced cold (reversal of functions) is different from cold-induced cold. Heat-induced cold presents with slight reversal followed by fever. Conversely, in cold-induced cold, there is no fever but cold limbs with a greater feeling of chill, a deep and thin pulse, along with loose stools and urination.

    Abnormal coldness in the hands and feet is referred to as "reversal." Reversal indicates a lack of harmony between yin and yang, resulting in cold limbs. When yang energy weakens and yin energy strengthens, the yin prevails over the yang, causing the yang pulse to reverse and therefore blockage to the hands and feet, resulting in coldness.[32p]
    In cases of cold and heat in febrile diseases, when there is more cold and less heat, the illness is likely to recover; conversely, if there is more heat and less cold, the illness worsens. However, one must carefully distinguish between cold and heat-induced extremities.

    Cold-induced extremities manifest as coldness in the limbs on the day of onset, with a pulse that is deep, weak, and not rapid. The feet often cramp, there is a preference for covering with clothing while lying down, a dislike for cold, or diarrhea with clear fluid, or a natural regulation of clear stools. Urination may be frequent, and external symptoms tend to be calm. If the pulse is deep and firm, but feels slow and weak upon pressure, it indicates cold-induced extremities. Appropriate remedies include Si Ni Decoction, Li Zhong Decoction, Tong Mai Si Ni Decoction, Dang Gui Si Ni Decoction, Dang Gui Si Ni with Fushen and Ginger Decoction, and Bai Tong with Pig Gall Bladder Decoction.

    Heat-induced extremities, on the other hand, are characterized by fever and headache on the first day of illness, accompanied by other Yang symptoms. It typically takes two to five days for the extremities to become cold. In cases of mixed heat and cold extremities, cold will emerge within half a day, following the fever, as deep heat is necessary to induce extremities. This will usually manifest after two to three days.[33p]
    If the fainting leads to fever, it is due to the slight heat. Although the pulse is deep and concealed, upon palpation it is slippery, indicating internal heat. The person may fear the heat, drink water, or wave their hands and feet, feeling restless and unable to sleep, with constipation and red urine, and showing signs of confusion. This indicates heat fainting, and remedies like Bai Hu and Cheng Qi should be used accordingly. Zhongjing says that in cases of chills and fever lasting one to five days, fainting must occur, and if there was prior fever, fainting will follow. The deeper the fainting, the deeper the heat; the milder the fainting, the milder the heat. If fainting that requires purging instead induces sweating, the mouth must be severely damaged and ulcerated. Additionally, if all symptoms are present with the four extremities feeling cold, it indicates blood and qi stagnation after purging, leading to coldness in the limbs. If the physician misidentifies this as a condition of yin, and administers heat-inducing drugs, disaster will follow swiftly. Generally, in heat fainting, the pulse must be deep and slippery, with sweat on the head; even if the hands are cold, the fingertips may occasionally feel warm, and one should promptly apply Cheng Qi Decoction without hesitation. Any cold in the extremities pertains to fainting due to yin, and must not be purged or induced to sweat.[34p]
    When there is a need for warmth in the extremities or signs of sweat, it indicates that although the hands and feet feel cold and may occasionally warm up, the palms must be warm; this is not true reversal. This should be monitored. If the patient experiences chills and fever with a pale complexion, is unwell, and suddenly has no pulse in both hands or one hand, it is likely due to a real exhaustion of sweat. One should extensively wrap the hands and feet in cotton clothing to keep them warm and urgently take a recipe such as Schisandra decoction, or possibly a combination of Ephedra, Asarum, and Licorice decoction. At that time, there will likely be a significant sweat leading to relief.

    When evil qi is trapped in the chest, it can also cause cold extremities, but recognizing a pulse that suddenly becomes blocked is key. Zang-exhaustion is difficult to treat.

    Inquiring about the Shaoyin Four-Reversal Decoction and the Four-Reversal Powder, one might ask why there is a distinction. The answer is that, generally, in Shaoyin illness, one should not hastily use warming medicines. Although there may be a surface heat in Shaoyin disease, which Zhang Zhongjing termed late-onset fever, one can still use combinations like Ephedra and Asarum to induce sweating without turning it into a true Shaoyin syndrome. In today’s cases, when the extremities are cold but there is internal heat, Zhang Zhongjing recommends the Four-Reversal Powder. The Four-Reversal Decoction employs Aconite and Dried Ginger, while the Four-Reversal Powder focuses on reversing the cold from the extremities; patients might cough, feel palpitations, have difficulty urinating, experience abdominal pain, or suffer from diarrhea and heavy stools—all of these are signs of heat conditions.[35p]
    Fainting and Reversal

    The energy reverses and rushes upward due to the upward heat of fire. The bending and stretching are not convenient; thus, fainting and reversal are stubborn and fixed. The cold water (yin) leads to clarity, hence, when ill with cold, the limbs become cold and reverse, leading to a constraint that is solid and rigid, causing difficulty in stretching and bending. Therefore, in winter, the pulse is heavy, short, and firm, reflecting the symptoms of this illness. If an illness of cold is still mild and has not yet reached fainting and reversal, it cannot be mistaken for heat. Likewise, if there is severe heat leading to yang fainting, it should not be interpreted as cold.

    For yin fainting, the original pulse and symptoms are all indicative of yin conditions: the body feels cool with no thirst, the pulse is slow, thin, and weak, with no evidence of yang conditions. For yang fainting, the original pulse and symptoms indicate yang conditions: extreme heat leads to reversal, and at times returns to warmth; even in fainting, there is agitation and thirst, with the body hot and pulse rapid. If yang fainting is very profound to the point of the body being cold with faint signs of a yin pulse that seems about to cease, it merely indicates extreme heat leading to a desire for death.[36p]
    The common people mistakenly believe that transformation into a Yin disease occurs, claiming that the interplay of Yin and Yang, heat and cold, is unpredictable. They uphold the notion that Yang is associated with life while Yin corresponds to death, urgently applying fire and warming herbs to stimulate the surface and internal warmth, thus supporting Yang energy, resulting in a survival rate of one in ten. This leads to a widespread fear of Yin conditions, causing those with suspected Yin diseases to be urgently warmed, out of fear that failure to act will invite misfortune. Yet they overlook that those with severe heat illnesses rarely escape this condition.

    They are unaware that the balance of Yin and Yang is what constitutes the Dao, while excess Yin or Yang results in illness. Yin and Yang achieve harmony through balance; imbalance causes disease. All things arise from the combination of Yin and Yang; therefore, excessive Yin cannot persist, and isolated Yang cannot thrive. When Yang energy is excessively strong and Yin energy is excessively weak, Yang becomes stagnant, leading to a tilt between Yin and Yang that prevents circulation. This results in cold extremities, known as Yang collapse. Thus, Zhang Zhongjing stated: "When heat is profound, the collapse is likewise profound; when heat is slight, the collapse is slight." He also noted: "Collapse should be addressed from below; once the heat inside is eliminated, the collapse will improve."[37p]
    Thus, when the disease heat is severe, there is a corresponding coldness. Moreover, if there is loss of lower energy, the heat worsens and manifests as a yin condition, not a transformation into a cold disease. The transmission and transformation of disease refer to the flow of pathological factors affecting the internal and external, upper and lower pathways of the body, rather than a mere reversal between cold and heat or yin and yang. The principle states: when yin and yang are balanced, there is harmony; when imbalanced, there is disease. For example, if yang is strong and yin is weak leading to heat, should it really transform into cold, it would be like when heat dissipates and cold arises, resulting in a balance of yin and yang which should lead to recovery. How could it become a cold disease? Although the discussion on malaria mentions that when yin prevails there is cold, and when yang prevails there is heat, it means that when interior energy and external heat are combined, there is yang predominance leading to fever; and when external energy and heat are combined, there is yin predominance leading to cold shivering. Due to superficial energy being weak and interior energy being hot, excess can be harmful, so counteractions are needed, hence the shivering. In general, it fundamentally stems from heat, not a cold disease.[38p]
    In cases of cold damage with alternating chills and fever, if the evil heat is superficial, it obstructs the right qi, hence the aversion to cold; if the evil heat is deep within, the evil is severe and unrestrained, leading to a disfavor of cold while the aversion turns toward heat. The interplay of exterior and interior continues, resulting in the alternation of chills and fever. This condition does not unify between exterior and interior, hence it differs from malaria where the chills and fever are mild; they arise from the transmission of heat to yin and yang on the surface, rather than a change in the yin and yang of the disease itself. Sometimes, if the disease is heat and the cold attack is excessive, the yang qi becomes weakened and yin qi increases excessively, leading to a subsequent condition of cold; this arises from overdosing on medication rather than natural fluctuations of cold and heat.

    When the six qi become chaotic and manifest as disease, they do so by combining and coexisting as one illness. Wind, heat, and dryness often combine together, as do cold and dampness; however, it is rare for dissimilar natures to combine. When there is severe control leading to a combination, it is a manifestation of deficiency. For instance, when fire heat is extreme and water is used to control it, it may result in shivering; generally, this is due to excessive heat rather than cold qi, thus thirst arises indicating heat within, while shivering causes the desire to drink cold. Similarly, when fire refines metal and the heat is extreme leading to transformation into water, even though it becomes water, it is still fundamentally due to intense heat resulting in the essence of metal.[39p]
    If there is excessive dryness and heat leading to stagnation in the intestines and stomach, or if drinking too much cold liquid causes obstruction and fullness, and retained fluids fail to transform and nourish due to extreme cold accumulating in the stomach, then excessive dryness and heat obstruct the chest and abdomen, causing bloating and incessant thirst, which in turn leads to cold pain in the stomach and chest, along with vomiting of watery substances, making it difficult to swallow. Attempting to quench thirst by drinking more water leads to increased fullness and pain and worsens the vomiting, yet the thirst remains unquenched. If one refrains from drinking, the unbearable thirst creates restlessness and distress, making one wish for death. Mismanagement can lead to death, and neglecting treatment is also quite difficult.

    In such cases, we typically administer Da Chengqi Decoction hot to facilitate swallowing, which can relieve the stagnation in the intestines and stomach. This helps to transform and nourish the retained fluids, dispersing cold and dampness, thus allowing the stomach and intestines to regain moisture. As the heat subsides, the distress and thirst along with the bloating and vomiting cease, leading to quick relief. However, the causes of the illness must be understood. It is uncommon for a condition primarily caused by heat to transform into cold. Generally, when yang is strong, the pulse should be strong and rapid, accompanied by body heat and thirst; when heat becomes excessive, it leads to yang collapse.[40p]
    When it reaches the extreme, the body becomes cold and the pulse weakens, resembling symptoms of yin conditions, leading to a pulse cessation and death. Therefore, when a yang illness exhibits a yin pulse, it indicates the pulse is nearly gone, suggesting a fatal condition. Even if the illness is intensely hot, if it persists, there must be cold extremities and a weak pulse, eventually resulting in a cold body and pulse cessation followed by death. This could arise from the illness initially being too hot, from excessive treatment leading to worsening symptoms, from a loss of cold medicine for regulation, from improper treatment methods, or from mistakenly taking hot medicine or applying excessive heat, resulting in extreme heat causing yang collapse. In such cases, administering cold medicines like the Chaihu Decoction can reduce the heat and restore the balance, alleviating the collapse. It is crucial to avoid using harmful hot and toxic drugs like silver powder or croton seeds, as they will deplete yin energy and exhaust body fluids, exacerbating dry heat and causing serious complications such as breathlessness, abdominal pain, persistent diarrhea, blood overflow, or various heat transformation symptoms. Such remedies are intended for breaking up hard accumulations, not for addressing heat or nourishing yin. The ancients noted that treating febrile diseases with hot, toxic preparations is akin to using a blade to harm someone.[41p]
    There was a case of excess yang where the person did not improve, resulting in a cold body and weak pulse, resembling a condition of yin. Mistakenly, hot medicines were administered, worsening the condition to the point that the body was cold, the pulse was weak and almost absent, with only a slight warmth in the chest and heart, leading to faintness and confusion, making the patient unable to speak. The doctor intended to use warming medicines to urgently revive the yang, fearing the disappearance of yang would lead to death. However, they did not realize this was caused by excessive heat disrupting the downward flow, and subsequently supplementing warmth exacerbated the issue. If more hot medicines were used to support the yang energy, the yin would suddenly deplete, resulting in the death of the yang energy as well; where would the yang energy be generated from then?

    Some might ask: Why not urgently promote a downward flow? The answer is that if the yang is excessive and attacks the yin, leading the yin to deplete first, the yang will also be exhausted. At this moment, if one attempts to induce a downward flow, both yin and yang would cease, resulting in immediate death; thus, neglecting the situation would also lead to death. However, if the condition reaches a certain point, a gentle intervention can save them; in this case, one should use cold medicines to nourish the yin and slightly reduce the yang, making sure there is no violent purging. If the yin energy can gradually recover, salvation is possible. It is advisable to use a cooling remedy, as this can encourage the gradual recovery of yin energy. How can this be determined? It can be gauged by observing a gradual increase in warmth in the chest and heart, along with the gradual re-establishing of the pulse.[42p]
    Throughout the day, there are three treatments; the pulse indicates a significantly deep and rapid state, the body surface is warm, yet there is a reversal of vital energy. There is a good tolerance for water, and sometimes responses to inquiries are delusional, with a strong tongue making it difficult to speak. By using the Decoction for Regulating the Stomach and Resolving Qi, one may achieve sweating and recovery. The so-called cold medicines can actually nourish the pulse and warm the body, because of a condition where yang is solid but yin is weak, leading towards death; the body turns cold and the pulse becomes faint. Now, by using cold medicines to nourish yin and reduce yang, one can avoid death.

    Generally, when treating illness, it is essential to clarify the root and the branch. The branch is the initial symptom, while the root is the fundamental cause. Thus, the classics say that the initial illness is the root and subsequent illness is the branch; the root and branch are interrelated, and treatment should first address the urgent symptoms. It is also said that the six qi serve as the root, while the three yin and three yang are branches; thus, the pathogenic qi is the root, while the affected meridians and organs are branches. The subtlety of root and branch, treating them accordingly cannot be overlooked. Hence, the classics state that knowing what opposes and aligns is crucial; when the appropriate course is taken, there are no gaps.

    To clearly understand root and branch ensures that all measures are apt. Ignorance of root and branch is called acting blindly. The interplay of yin and yang, and the relationship between root and branch is the pathway to knowledge. Is this not its principle?

    In cases of one yang and one yin, if illness manifests with fright, back pain, and sighing, it is termed wind reversal. This is because the stomach (earth) and liver (wood) interact, as wood overcomes earth. When wind overcomes dampness and does not control kidney water, it causes a reversal upwards, with the herb Yuan Zhi identified as its chief remedy.[43p]
    The Theory of Huang Liao
    (By Jin Cheng Wuji)

    What explains the situation of the Four Reverses in Cold Damage? The "Four Reverses" refers to the limbs being reversed and not warm. Accumulated cold leads to coldness and accumulated warmth leads to heat; these conditions do not arise in just a day or night, but develop gradually over time. When Cold Damage first occurs, the evil is present in the skin. When the taiyang and yangming channels are affected, the whole body will feel hot; when the shaoyin and taiyin channels are impacted, the hands and feet will feel warm on their own, indicating the exterior evil has become milder and wishes to transmit inward. The classic states: "In the case of Cold Damage, if after four or five days the hands and feet are warm and thirst arises, the Xiao Chai Hu Decoction should be administered." This indicates that the evil in the taiyang has transmitted to the shaoyang. When the pulse is superficial and the hands and feet are warm on their own, it shows the condition is associated with the taiyin, meaning the shaoyang evil has transmitted to the taiyin. It is understood that when the evil energy is halfway between the exterior and interior, the hands and feet do not feel hot but remain warm. When the evil transmits to the shaoyin, it indicates that the interior condition is severe; even though it has not yet manifested as cold extremities, the hands and feet become even less warm, which is identified as the Four Reverses. If it reaches the jueyin stage, the hands and feet will feel cold.[44p]
    The Classic text states: When a person has a condition characterized by cold limbs—whether by coughing, palpitations, difficulty urinating, abdominal pain, or severe diarrhea—this is diagnosed as a "Four Reversals" condition. The treatment is "Four Reversal Powder," which consists of four ingredients: Chai Hu, Zhi Shi, Shao Yao, and Gan Cao. All of these are cold in nature yet specifically treat the Four Reversal illness, indicating that this condition is not merely a sign of excessive coldness.

    Additionally, there are also "Four Reversal Decoctions" which treat the coldness in the hands and feet using warming herbs like Gan Jiang and Fu Zi, which is very effective against the illness. If the hands and feet generate warmth but then turn cold, this condition is caused by an internal disturbance, and the "Four Reversal Powder" shall treat it. If one begins to experience chilly hands and feet that do not warm up, this indicates that the Yin channels are afflicted and Yang Qi is insufficient; "Four Reversal Decoction" can be used to warm it.

    It is crucial to recognize this to avoid misunderstandings. The conditions of Four Reversals and cold extremities are similar but not the same. The text states: "Any severe case of Four Reversal cold should not be treated as diarrhea," indicating that Four Reversals and cold are distinctly different. Severe symptoms accompanied by vomiting, diarrhea, and irritability suggest serious danger in the case of Four Reversals. Diagnosis should be conducted with care and thoroughness!

    Regarding cold in febrile diseases, how can it be clarified? Cold indicates a worse condition than Four Reversals. The text notes: "Coldness arises when Yin and Yang energies do not correspond effectively." Coldness manifests as reversing coldness in the hands and feet.[45p]
    It is said that when the yang energy sinks inward and the heat energy reverses and stagnates, the hands and feet become cold. The classics state that if one has a cold damage for one or two days and experiences reversal after four or five days, then fever must arise. The previous heat will inevitably be followed by reversal. The deeper the reversal, the deeper the heat; the milder the reversal, the milder the heat. Thus, it is known that when there is sinking inward, the hands and feet are in reversal. In lesser yin diseases, there is only reversal without sweating, and if one forces sweating, it will certainly move the blood, but one does not know through which channel it will exit, either through the mouth and nose or from the eyes. This is termed "lower reversal with upper exhaustion," and it also refers to activating the heat. If the fever comes first and is followed by reversal, it means the heat is hidden within; if reversal comes first and is followed by fever, it means the yin has receded and the yang energy has recovered. If one initially experiences reversal, it signifies that the yang energy is insufficient while the yin energy is dominant. Generally, reversal is governed by the yin, and cold is prevalent, with distinctions of progress and retreat. The classic states: If one has reversal for five days, there will also be heat for five days. If after six days there is no reversal, recovery will occur. If fever lasts for four days and reversal lasts for three days, recovery will ensue if fever returns for four days with minimal reversal and much heat. If there is reversal for four days, fever for three days, followed by reversal for five days, the condition progresses.[46p]
    When cold is abundant and heat is scarce, it indicates the retreat of yang energy, thus leading to progression. If illness reaches the Jueyin, the meridians are completely exhausted. At such a time, yang energy prevails over yin; hence, there is little cold and much heat, and the illness improves. However, if yin energy exceeds, and yang cannot recover, there will be much cold and little heat, causing the illness to reverse. Cold is the arrival of yin energy, while heat represents the recovery of yang energy. When it comes to diarrhea, it is said that there will be cold first, then heat will emerge, and the diarrhea will surely stop, indicating that the cold must recover leading to the cessation of diarrhea. Cold is the manifestation of heat, as yang energy recovers, leading to the inevitable cessation of diarrhea. Heat, in turn, signifies the return of cold, implying that yin energy is once again prevailing, thus causing the recurrence of diarrhea.

    The yang energies reside within the chest; when evil energies reside in the chest, stagnation occurs, preventing yang energy from dispersing, leading to coldness in the hands and feet. The texts state: "When there is cold in the hands and feet, the pulse is intermittently tense, evil is obstructed in the chest, the heart feels full and distressed, and hunger does not allow for eating; illness in the chest should be expelled." This is the manifestation of excessive yin. If there is even worse cold leading to curling up, the yin energy is extremely strong and difficult to control. The texts say: "In lesser yin disorders, if there is aversion to cold, curling of the body, diarrhea, and cold in the hands and feet, it is untreatable." This indicates that cold is a reversal; can divine elixirs create life?[47p]
    The Confucian Attitude Towards Parents

    On the Condition of Syncope in Recent Times

    Syncope describes a state where the hands and feet, as well as below the knees, can feel either cold or hot. The world generally holds that "kicking leg disease" is an ailment caused by cold and dampness, yet "The Internal Classic" does not mention this condition. Wang Taifu also stated that there was originally no such disease; it was later defined by "The Book of Broad Treatments." In ancient texts, what we call "kicking leg disease" refers to the condition of syncope. However, syncope should be differentiated into two types, which are then subdivided into five organ categories. The two types are cold syncope and hot syncope. When yang energy is weak below, it leads to cold syncope; when yin energy is weak below, it results in hot syncope. Hot syncope manifests as hot hands and feet, while cold syncope manifests as cold hands and feet. Yang meridians originate from the surface of the toes, while yin meridians begin from the soles of the feet. When yang energy is strong, there is heat in the lower parts; when yin energy is strong, there is cold. Furthermore, it’s said that yang governs the exterior and syncope occurs in the interior, while yin governs the interior and syncope occurs in the exterior. This is because the energies of yin and yang are reversed and move upwards. In spring and summer, yang is abundant and yin is scarce; in autumn and winter, yin strengthens and yang weakens. People may rely on their vigor and indulge during autumn and winter, leading to a depletion of internal yang and a surplus of essence that flows downward, allowing evil energy to rise. When yang energy declines, true essence is also exhausted, which causes the body not to nourish; thus, yin energy operates alone, resulting in cold hands and feet, which is classified as cold syncope.[48p]
