The foundation of vital energy primarily lies in the kidneys; thus, when the lesser yin is insufficient, it results in "厥." Furthermore, the essay on regulating the meridians states that a deficiency of will leads to "厥." The section on the spirit indicates that a deficiency in kidney energy leads to "厥." Observing these discussions, it is clear that the essence of "厥" is not related to wind. Therefore, for treating this condition, one should emphasize methods that are not based on wind symptoms. The essay on regulating the meridians indicates that both energy and blood can be deficient, revealing an imbalance of yin and yang. If both energy and blood travel upwards, it indicates a deficiency of yin below and a lack of root in the spirit, resulting in the separation of yin and yang, which may cause sudden death. If the condition is slight, recovery can be achieved; if it is severe, the situation is critical.[77p]

    此正时人所谓卒倒暴仆之中风，亦即痰火上壅之中风，而不知实由于下虚也。然上实者假实也，其有甚者，亦宜稍为清理。下虚者真虚也，若无实邪可据，则速当峻补其下。　　观阳明脉解篇之连经连脏，本以厥逆为言，何其明显平正！盖连经者病在肌表，故轻而生；连脏者病在根本，故重而死。既知此为厥逆，则凡卒倒暴仆等证，其非风也可知，而河间诸公皆以中腑中脏为言，则是风非风，始混乱而莫辨矣。　　详大奇论、解精微论二篇云：脉至如喘者，谓脉之急促如喘，此血气败乱之候，故致暴厥不言，即今人所谓中风不语之属也。[78p]

    This is precisely what people today refer to as an abrupt fall or collapse due to a stroke, which is also a stroke caused by phlegm-heat obstructing the upper body, while failing to realize that it actually stems from a deficiency in the lower body. However, the condition of the upper body being 'full' is only a false fullness, and in severe cases, it should be slightly cleared. The deficiency in the lower body is a true emptiness; if there are no pathogenic factors to address, then one must promptly strengthen the lower body decisively.

    In observing the passages of the Yangming classic regarding the linking of channels and organs, it is stated that 'reversal of qi' is significant, which is quite evident and straightforward! The linking of channels indicates that the illness lies in the muscles, hence it is light and produces symptoms; whereas, the linking of organs indicates that the illness lies at the root, thus it is heavy and fatal. Having recognized this as a reversal of qi, it can be discerned that symptoms like abrupt falls and collapses are not truly strokes, but various scholars in Hejian refer to the central organs, which leads to confusion between true and false strokes, making it difficult to distinguish.

    The detailed discussions in the Great Righteousness Treatise and the Subtle Analysis Treatise state: "When the pulse reaches a state resembling panting, it indicates a pulse that is rapid and urgent like breathlessness, reflecting a condition of chaotic blood and qi, hence resulting in sudden reversal and inability to speak," which aligns with what people today refer to as a 'silent stroke.'[78p]

    云阳并于上，阴并于下，此即上热下寒水火不交之候，故为目无所见，即中风昏眩之属也。不语者责在肺肾，昏眩者责在肝脾。暂见者气复则苏，阴败者最危之候。俱当按法如前而救其本。　　详终始篇论厥云：暴清即暴冷也，若裂若切，谓其懊憹痛楚，莫可名状，此即所谓躁扰烦乱之中风也。有火者多温热而脉洪大，宜清阴中之火；有痰者多喘壅而脉滑实，宜开上焦之痰；无火无痰，多寒凉而脉濇弱，宜补其元气。凡证有若此而兼之昏乱不醒者，此真连脏之甚者也，多不可治。　　详生气通天论云：煎厥者即热厥之类，其因烦劳而病积于夏，亦今云暑风之属也。[79p]

    In Yunyang, the upper part is hot and the lower part is cold; this indicates a condition where water and fire do not interact, leading to a state of blindness, akin to dizziness caused by wind. Those who cannot speak are suffering issues related to the lungs and kidneys, while those who are dizzy have problems linked to the liver and spleen. For those who temporarily regain consciousness, recovery can occur when the Qi returns; however, if the Yin deteriorates, it is a very dangerous condition. All should be treated according to the previous principles to address the root cause.

    In the discussion of the "End and Beginning" chapter, it states: sudden clarity refers to sudden coldness; if it feels like being split or severed, it is described as painful and indescribable, which aligns with the so-called confusion and disturbance caused by wind. Those with heat often experience warmth and a strong pulse, thus it is advisable to clear the fire within the Yin. Those with phlegm often suffer from wheezing and have a slippery pulse, thus it is necessary to relieve the phlegm in the upper jiao. For those without fire or phlegm, they tend to feel cold and have a weak pulse, hence it is necessary to tonify the primordial Qi. In cases with such symptoms coupled with confusion and loss of consciousness, this represents a severe condition involving multiple organs, often difficult to treat.

    The "Connecting Qi to the Heavens" chapter explains that convulsions due to heat are a type of heat stroke, caused by overexertion accumulating during summer, which can now be referred to as heat wind.[79p]

    若见抽搐痰涎卒倒者，当即以前暑风之法治之。　　薄厥者，急迫相薄之谓，因于大怒，即气厥血厥之属，治法如后。　　详通评虚实论云：膏粱之疾，即酒色之伤脾肾之病也；暴忧之病，即悲忧伤肺之属也；内气暴薄，即郁怒伤肝之属也。凡此皆内伤之病。其有不从内而外中于风者，则必留着经络，故为消瘦痛痹之病。是可见内伤外感之辨，其不可混言有如此。　　详逆顺肥瘦篇冲脉之义，则上自头，下自足，后自背，前自腹，凡五脏六腑十二经脉，无所不禀，故称为五脏六腑十二经脉之海，夫海为百川之宗，凡诸经发源之处，即皆有会合之义，其于通身血气盛衰，皆归乎此可知也。[80p]

    If one sees a person suddenly collapse with convulsions and phlegm, they should immediately treat them using methods for heat stroke. "Thin prickle" refers to a situation of acute pressure caused by great anger, leading to conditions such as qi and blood stasis; the treatment approach should be as follows.

    According to the detailed analysis of deficiencies and excesses, diseases caused by rich foods and liquors harm the spleen and kidneys; diseases arising from sudden worries are related to the sadness that harms the lungs; internal qi being violently depleted relates to anger affecting the liver. All these are considered internal injuries. If there is an external wind causing harm rather than internal issues, it will certainly affect the meridians, leading to symptoms of emaciation and painful obstruction. Thus, the distinction between internal injuries and external attacks can be understood and should not be confused.

    In detail regarding the principles of reversal and order about fat and thin, the pathways run from the head down to the feet, from the back to the abdomen. All organs and meridians, including the five zang organs, six fu organs, and twelve meridians, are interconnected; thus, they are referred to as the sea of the five zang, six fu, and twelve meridians. The sea is the source of all rivers; hence, wherever the meridians originate, there is a sense of convergence. This understanding applies to the ebb and flow of blood and qi throughout the body.[80p]

    然冲脉起于胞中，即其经络之所，亦即其聚畜之所，故称为血海，亦称为命门，此即所谓根本之宅也。若素纵情欲，以致精气之源伤败于此，则厥脱暴仆等病，亦因于此。不然，则何以忽然仆倒而神形俱败，表里俱残，全无知觉，一至于此，是岂一经一脏之病之所致欤？于此察之，则实由冲脉崩败，必无疑矣。故凡治此者，欲舍根蒂而求其济，吾知其必无是理也！　　详缪刺论尸厥一证，乃外邪卒中之恶候。凡四时不正之气，及山魔土煞，五尸魇魅之属皆是也。[81p]

    The Chong Vessel originates in the womb, which is where its meridians converge and where vital energies accumulate. Hence, it is referred to as the Sea of Blood or the Gate of Life; this is what is called the fundamental abode. If one indulges in passions, leading to the depletion of the source of essence and energy, conditions such as syncope and sudden collapse will arise from this. Otherwise, how is it that one can suddenly fall, with both spirit and body in decline, utterly oblivious to surroundings? When it reaches this point, is it merely a disease of a single meridian or organ? Upon examination, it becomes clear that it is indeed due to the collapse of the Chong Vessel, without a doubt. Therefore, anyone who treats this by seeking relief without addressing the root cause, it is certain that such reasoning is flawed! Specifically regarding the discussion of the condition of shock from external evil influence, it is associated with sudden onset of malign conditions. This includes all forms of improper energies across the four seasons, as well as mountain spirits and soil demons, along with all sorts of phantoms and nightmares.[81p]

    犯之者忽然手足厥冷，肌肤寒栗，面目青黑，精神不守，或口噤妄言，痰涎壅塞，或头旋运倒，不省人事，即名尸厥、卒厥，宜用针法，具见本经。若用艾灸，则无如秦承祖灸鬼法，及华佗灸阳脱法为妙。凡用药之法，当知邪之所凑，必因气虚，故在本经即以左角之血余，用补五络之脱竭，其义可知。若此危急之际，非用参附回阳等药，何以挽回？若果邪气壅盛，胸膈不清，则不得不先为开通，然后调理，宜不换金正气散、流气饮、葱姜汤、苏合丸之类酌而主之。　　详方盛衰论言，气逆者即为厥也。凡阴阳之气，阳从左而升，阴从右而降，故阳病者左为甚，阴病者右为甚。以升者不升，降者不降，而逆其升降之气也。[82p]

    When someone suffers from this condition, their hands and feet suddenly become cold, their skin shivers, their complexion turns dark and pale, and their spirit is unsettled. They may speak nonsensically or be unable to speak, with phlegm obstructing their throat. They might also experience dizziness and lose consciousness; this is referred to as "corpse syncope" or "sudden syncope." Acupuncture should be employed, as detailed in the classic texts. If moxibustion is used, the methods of Qin Chengzu and Hua Tuo for moxibustion on the yang are particularly effective.

    In all medicinal practices, one must understand that the presence of evils is due to qi deficiency; therefore, in the classic texts, it is mentioned to use blood from the left side to replenish the Five Meridians that are depleted, which is clear in meaning. In such dangerous moments, without employing herbs like ginseng and Aconite to restore yang, how can one recover? If the evil qi is overwhelming and the chest is obstructed, one must first clear the passages before regulating. One should primarily use formulas like Jin Zheng Qi San, Liu Qi Yin, green onion and ginger soup, or Su He Wan.

    A discussion on the strength and weakness of formulas concludes that counteracting the path of qi is the same as syncope. The interplay of yin and yang qi is such that yang rises from the left and yin descends from the right; therefore, for yang illnesses, the left side is more severe, and for yin illnesses, the right side is more severe. When the rising does not rise and the descending does not descend, it is the reversal of the natural flow of qi.[82p]

    又人之生气，必自下而升，故老人之气已衰于下，而从上者为顺；少壮之气，先盛于下，而从下者为顺。若以老人而神衰于上，其所终之气可知；少壮而形衰于下，其所始之气可知，皆逆候也。及其为病而一上不下，此其根本已亏，故寒厥到膝。少年以阳气方盛而阳衰若此，故秋冬当死；老人以阳气本衰，而畏寒其常，故秋冬无虑。凡此厥逆之病，谓其阳若非阳，谓其阴若非阴，五脏隔绝，无征可验，若不能终其日者，盖甚言其雕敝难为也。再若人之妄梦，而有至迷乱昏绝者，此以心肾不交而精神散越，故为厥逆，有如此，亦总属少阴根本之病。[83p]

    The vitality of a person must ascend from below; therefore, the energy of the elderly has declined from below, and what arises from above is in accordance with nature. In contrast, the vitality of youth is initially strong from below, and what rises from below is in accordance with nature. If an old person’s spirit declines from above, the energy at their end is predictable; when the young person’s body weakens from below, the energy at their beginning is predictable as well, both are cases of reversal. When one becomes ill and cannot rise or fall, it indicates that their foundation has deteriorated, hence the cold and extremities reach to the knees. The youth, with their yang energy still vigorous, face decomposition during autumn and winter; the elderly, with their yang energy inherently diminished and more sensitive to cold, therefore have no worries in autumn and winter. All these diseases of inversion, where yang appears not to be yang and yin seems not to be yin, create a separation of the five organs, leaving no evidence to verify. If one cannot complete their days, it signifies their serious decline. Furthermore, in dreams where one is utterly confused and disoriented, this results from the heart and kidneys not communicating, causing the spirit to scatter and stray, thus leading to inversion. Such conditions are fundamentally linked to the roots of the lesser yin.[83p]

    　　详厥论之寒厥热厥，虽皆以手足为言，而实以阴阳之败乱为言也。故寒厥言夺于所用，热厥言因于数醉。正以阴阳之气，无不起于手足，故凡厥之将作，则寒热麻痹，必先由手足而起。及其甚也，则变出百端，或五脏六腑，各有其证如此。然则手足之厥，特其形见之征兆耳，而见微知着，自当因标而虑本也。　　详仲景论厥逆，颇与《内经》有异。盖以手足言之，在《内经》则有寒厥热厥之分，在仲景则单以逆冷者为厥。再以邪正言之，在《内经》则论在元气，故其变出百端，而在气在血，俱有危证；在仲景则论在邪气，故单据手足，而所畏者，则在阴进而阳退也。观成无己曰：厥为阴之盛也，义可知矣。[84p]

    The discussion of cold and hot collapse (jue) involves the hands and feet as terms, but essentially speaks to the disorder of yin and yang. Cold collapse represents a loss due to usage, while hot collapse arises from excessive drinking. This is because the energies of yin and yang invariably manifest in the hands and feet; thus, when collapse is about to occur, cold and heat numbness must first emerge from the hands and feet. When it becomes severe, it may manifest in various ways, potentially affecting the five organs and six bowels, each presenting its own symptoms. Therefore, the collapse of the hands and feet serves primarily as a visible sign, and by recognizing slight indications, one should consider the underlying causes.

    Examining Zhang Zhongjing's views on reverse collapse, there are notable differences from the "Inner Canon." In the "Inner Canon," discussions concerning the hands and feet distinguish between cold and hot collapse, whereas Zhang Zhongjing focuses solely on the aspect of cold reversal as a form of collapse. Furthermore, concerning the discussion of evil and righteous energies, the "Inner Canon" addresses the original qi, hence the manifold symptoms, encompassing both qi and blood, which all bear critical signs; in contrast, Zhang Zhongjing emphasizes the role of evil qi, considering the hands and feet only, with fears directed towards the descent of yin and the retreat of yang. Cheng Wujide states: collapse signifies the predominance of yin, which is understandable.[84p]

    　　　　　论证

    　　厥逆之证，危证也。盖厥者尽也，逆者乱也，即气血败乱之谓也。故《内经》特重而详言之。即云卒厥暴厥者，皆厥逆之总名也。如云寒厥热厥者，分厥逆之阴阳也。如云连经连脏者，论厥逆之死生也。再若诸经脏腑之辨，亦既详矣。叉近世犹有气厥、血厥，痰厥，酒厥，蛔厥等证，亦无非本之经义。观《内经》诸纶，已极颢明，奈何后人犹不能察，凡遇此证，则悉认之为中风，竟不知厥逆为何证，而通作风治，害孰甚焉！余深悲之，故于前非风门悉力辨正。至于治此之法，即当以前非风证治，互相参用，正所以治厥逆也。其有未尽等证，仍列于后条。[85p]

    Argument

    The signs of reversal (or counterflow) are those of danger. The term 'reversal' signifies a complete disruption or chaos, representing the disorder of qi and blood. This is why the "Inner Canon" places special emphasis on it and explains it in detail. It states that sudden and violent reversals are both general names for this condition. For instance, terms like cold reversal and hot reversal differentiate the yin and yang aspects of the condition. When mentioning connected channels and organs, it discusses the life and death aspects of reversal. Moreover, the distinctions among the various channels and organs have also been elaborated upon.

    Additionally, in recent times, there are still signs such as qi reversal, blood reversal, phlegm reversal, alcohol reversal, and ascaris reversal, all of which are fundamentally based on these principles. Observing the teachings of the "Inner Canon," they appear to be quite clear; however, later generations still fail to recognize this. Whenever they encounter these signs, they tend to label them all as a stroke, unaware of what reversal truly signifies, thus treating them as wind disorders, which can lead to greater harm. I am deeply saddened by this, which is why I have made efforts to clarify previous misinterpretations of wind conditions.

    As for the treatment of these conditions, it should be approached as treating the previous non-wind signs, using them in conjunction. This is precisely how one should address reversal. Any remaining similar signs will still be listed in subsequent sections.[85p]

    　　　　　论治

    　　凡寒厥者，必四肢清凉，脉沉微不数，或虽数而无力，或畏寒喜热，引衣自覆，或下利清谷，形证多惺惺。虽此类皆属寒证，然似热非热之证犹多。故凡以手足见厥而脉证俱经无实热者，悉寒厥之无疑也。热厥者必先多热证，脉沉滑而数，畏热喜冷，扬手掉足，或烦躁不宁，大便秘赤，形证多昏冒。凡治此二者，即当以非风门治寒治热之法主之。至若伤寒厥证，其阴其阳，亦当以此法为辨。但伤寒之厥，辨在邪气，故寒厥宜温，热厥宜攻也。[86p]

    Discussion on Treatment

    In cases of cold extremities, the limbs must be cool, with a pulse that is deep, faint, and infrequent; or, even if frequent, it is weak. The patient may fear cold and prefer warmth, covering themselves with clothing, or may experience diarrhea of clear fluids, and the physical symptoms are generally weak. Although these cases all pertain to cold syndromes, there are many conditions that resemble heat but are not actually heat-related. Therefore, whenever there is cold extremity with pulse and symptoms not indicative of real heat, it is certainly cold extremity without doubt.

    Hot extremities must first show numerous heat-related symptoms, with a pulse that is deep, slippery, and rapid; the patient fears heat and prefers coolness, may wave their hands and kick their feet, or feel restless, with constipation and dark stools, and the physical symptoms are often marked by confusion or stupor.

    When treating these two conditions, one should apply methods distinct from treating cold and heat conditions associated with wind. As for the case of cold extremities resulting from cold damage, both its yin and yang aspects should be discerned using this method. However, in cases of cold extremities due to cold damage, the distinction lies in the pathogenic qi, hence cold extremities should be treated with warming methods, while hot extremities should be addressed with purging methods.[86p]

    《内经》之厥重在元气，故热厥当补阴，寒厥当补阳也。二者之治，不可不察！　　气厥之证有二，以气虚气实皆能厥也。气虚卒倒者，必其形气索然，色清白，身微冷，脉微弱，此气脱证也，宜参、芪、归、朮、地黄、枸杞、大补元煎之属，甚者以回阳饮、独参汤之类主之。气实而厥者，其形气愤然勃然，脉沉弦而滑，胸膈喘满，此气逆证也。大怒则形气绝而血菀于上，即此类也，治宜以排气饮，或四磨饮，或八味顺气散、苏合香丸之类先顺其气，然后随其虚实而调理之。[87p]

    In the "Neijing," the essential focus is on the primordial qi. Therefore, for heat syncope, one must supplement yin, and for cold syncope, one must supplement yang. The treatment of both cases cannot be overlooked!

    The symptoms of qi syncope are of two types, as both qi deficiency and qi excess can lead to syncope. In cases of sudden collapse due to qi deficiency, the body will appear weak, the color will be pale, the limbs will feel slightly cold, and the pulse will be weak—this indicates a loss of qi. One should use remedies such as ginseng, astragalus, angelica, poria, rehmannia, goji berries, or great rejuvenation decoctions; in severe cases, remedies like Huayan Decoction or Ginseng Decoction should be used.

    In cases of syncope due to qi excess, the body will appear agitated, the pulse will be deep, taut, and slippery, and there will be fullness in the chest and diaphragm—this indicates a reversal of qi. In cases of great anger, the body and qi may collapse, leading to blood pooling above; this is related. Treatment should include dispersing Qi Decoction, Four Molar Decoction, Eight Flavors Tranquilizing Powder, or Su He Xiang Pill to first normalize the qi, then subsequently regulate according to the condition of deficiency or excess.[87p]

    若因怒伤气逆，气旋去而真气受损者，气本不实也，若素多忧郁恐畏而气怯气陷者，其虚尤可知，若以此类而用行气开滞等剂则误矣。　　血厥之证有二，以血脱血逆皆能厥也。血脱者，如大崩大吐，或产血尽脱，则气亦随之而脱，故致卒仆暴死。宜先掐人中，或烧酢炭以收其气，急用人参一二两煎汤灌之，但使气不尽脱，必渐苏矣；然后因其寒热，徐为调理，此所谓血脱益气也。若不知此而但用血分等药，则几微之气，忽而散失，阴无所主，无生机矣。其或有用寒凉以止血者，必致败绝阳气，适足以速其死耳。[88p]

    If one becomes angry and harms the qi, causing it to be reversed and thus impairing the true qi, it indicates that the qi was initially weak. If one is prone to much anxiety and fear, leading to a timid and trapped qi, this weakness becomes even more apparent. If one uses methods meant to regulate the qi and resolve stagnation in such cases, it would be a mistake.

    There are two types of blood stasis: one caused by blood loss and the other by blood reversal, both of which can lead to stasis. Blood loss occurs in cases of severe bleeding or excessive blood loss during childbirth, leading to a loss of qi as well, hence causing sudden collapse and death. In such cases, one should first pinch the philtrum or burn vinegar with charcoal to gather the qi, and urgently administer one or two taels of ginseng decoction to restore the qi, ensuring it does not completely escape; this will lead to gradual recovery. Then, according to the conditions of cold or heat, one may proceed to regulate it accordingly; this is called replenishing the qi after blood loss.

    If one does not understand this and merely uses medicines for the blood, even a small amount of qi could suddenly dissipate, leaving the yin with nothing to support it, and thus there would be no vitality. If one considers using cold and cooling methods to stop the bleeding, it will certainly damage the yang qi, hastening death.[88p]

    血逆者，即经所云血之与气并走于上之谓，又曰大怒则形气绝而血菀于上之类也。夫血因气逆，必须先理其气，气行则血无不行也。宜通瘀煎或化肝煎之类主之，俟血行气舒，然后随证调理。　　凡一时痰涎壅塞，气闭昏愦，药食俱不能通，必先宜或吐或开以治其标，此不得不先救其急也。但觉痰气稍开，便当治其病本。如因火生痰者，宜清之降之；因风寒生痰者，宜散之温之；因湿生痰者，宜燥之利之；因脾虚生痰者，自宜补脾；因肾虚生痰者，自宜补肾。此痰之不必治也，但治其所以生痰而痰自清矣。然犹有不可治痰者，恐愈攻愈虚而痰必愈甚也。[89p]

    Blood reversal refers to the phenomenon where blood and qi move together upwards, and it is also described as a condition where intense anger causes the manifestation of qi to be disrupted, leading to blood accumulating above. When blood is affected by reverse qi, it is essential to first regulate the qi; when qi flows smoothly, blood will follow suit. It is advisable to use formulas like Tongyu Decoction or Huagan Decoction to address this condition and, once blood circulation is restored and qi is relaxed, to treat according to the specific symptoms.

    When phlegm and fluids obstruct the body, causing qi to become stagnant and mental confusion, and neither medication nor food can alleviate it, one must prioritize either inducing vomiting or relieving the blockage to address the urgent condition. Once the phlegm and qi have opened slightly, one should then treat the root cause of the illness. If phlegm is caused by heat, it should be cleared and driven down; if caused by wind and cold, it should be dispersed and warmed; if caused by dampness, it should be dried and regulated; if caused by spleen deficiency, the spleen should be strengthened; if caused by kidney deficiency, the kidneys should be nourished. Treating the underlying causes will allow the phlegm to clear naturally. However, there are cases where phlegm cannot be treated directly, as pushing too hard may worsen the condition and exacerbate the phlegm.[89p]

    诸治痰法，见前非风门治痰条中。　　酒厥之证，即经所云热厥之属也。又经云酒风者，亦此类也。凡纵饮无节之人，多有此病。方其血气正盛，力能胜之，不知酒害之何有，及其将衰，则酒之侮人，斯可畏耳。酒病极多，莫知所出，其为酒厥，则全似中风，轻者犹自知人，重者卒而运倒，忽然昏愦，或躁烦，或不语，或痰涎如涌，或气喘发热，或咳嗽，或吐血。但察其大便干燥，脉实喜冷者，此湿热上壅之证，宜以抽薪饮之类，疾降其火。[90p]

    Various methods for treating phlegm can be found in the previous section regarding the treatment of phlegm not caused by wind. The symptoms of "alcoholic syncope" correspond to those described as "heat syncope" in the classics. Furthermore, the classic also mentions "alcohol wind," which belongs to this category. Those who indulge in drinking without restraint often suffer from this illness. When their vital energy is strong and can overcome it, they do not recognize the harm of alcohol; but when they begin to weaken, the effects of alcohol become frightening. There are many ailments caused by alcohol, and their origins are unknown. When it comes to alcoholic syncope, it closely resembles a stroke: in mild cases, the person may still be aware, but in severe cases, they may suddenly collapse, become unresponsive, or exhibit sudden confusion, agitation, inability to speak, excessive phlegm, breathlessness, fever, cough, or even spitting blood. If one observes that the stools are dry and the pulse is strong and prefers cold, this indicates excess heat and dampness obstructing upward, and it is advisable to use methods like extracting the fuel (removing the underlying cause) and drinking to swiftly cool the fire.[90p]

    火之甚者，仍以梨浆饮、菉豆饮之属更迭进之，以解其毒。此证大忌辛燥等物，务使湿热渐退，神气稍复，然后用补阴等剂以善其后。其有大便不实，或无火证而脉见缓弱者，则不宜清火，但以二陈汤、六君子汤，或金水六君煎之类主之。若因酒伤阴，以致脾肾两虚而为厥脱者，非速救本源，终无济也。凡患此者，宜终身忌酒，勿使沾唇可也；若不知戒，再犯必难为矣。　　色厥之证有二，一曰暴脱，一曰动血也。凡色厥之暴脱者，必以其人本虚，偶因奇遇而悉力勉为者有之；或因相慕日久而纵竭情欲者亦有之。故于事后则气随精去，而暴脱不返。[91p]

    In cases of extreme heat, one should alternate with drinks made from pear syrup and mung bean to counteract the poison. It is crucial to avoid items that are spicy and dry, to gradually reduce damp heat and restore some energy, and only then use nourishing yin remedies for subsequent care. If there is constipation or a weak pulse without signs of heat, one should not clear heat but instead use remedies like Erchen Decoction, Liu Junzi Decoction, or Jinshui Liujun Decoction.

    If due to alcohol, the yin is harmed leading to the dual deficiency of spleen and kidney, and this results in syncope, one must promptly address the root cause; otherwise, there will be no benefit. Anyone suffering from this should avoid alcohol for life, ensuring they do not let it touch their lips; ignorance of this will make relapse very difficult.

    There are two types of symptoms of color loss: one is sudden collapse, and the other is blood movement. The sudden collapse of color is typically due to the person being fundamentally deficient, occasionally exerting themselves to the fullest in unusual circumstances; or it may occur after a prolonged indulgence in love and desire. Therefore, after such incidents, Qi departs along with essence, resulting in a sudden collapse that cannot be reversed.[91p]

    宜急掐人中，仍令阴人搂定，用口相对，务使暖气嘘通，以接其气，勿令放脱，以保其神；随速用独参汤灌之，或速灸气海数十壮，以复阳气，庶可挽回。但以临时慌张，焉知料理，故每致不救。然此以即病者言，所见诚不多也。其有不即病而病此者，则甚多也。又何以言之？以其精去于频，而气脱于渐，故每于房欲二三日之后，方见此证。但因其病不在即，故不以此为病，兼之人多讳此，而不知中年之后，多有因此而病者，是皆所谓色厥也，奈时师不能察而每以中风毙之耳。[92p]

    One should urgently press the Ren Zhong point, and have the individual embrace tightly, facing each other, ensuring that warm breath circulates between them to connect their vital energy, and not allow the energy to escape, in order to preserve the spirit. Then, quickly administer Duhua Decoction or apply strong moxibustion to the Qihai point several times to restore the Yang energy, which might help revive them. However, due to the urgency of the situation, how can one be meticulous in treatment? Thus, it often results in failure to save them. This discussion is specifically about those who are in immediate distress, and indeed, such cases are not many. Yet, there are many who suffer from latent conditions. How do I know this? Because their essence diminishes over time, and their vital energy gradually depletes. Therefore, symptoms often appear two or three days after engaging in sexual activity. But since the problem does not manifest immediately, it is not viewed as an illness. Moreover, many people are reluctant to talk about this, unaware that after middle age, many fall ill because of it; this is what is referred to as "color and syncope." Unfortunately, the practitioners of the time cannot discern this and simply attribute it to strokes.[92p]

    凡治此者，单宜培补命门，或水或火，当以非风门治法第三条者主之。　　又色厥之动血者，以其血气并走于上，亦血厥之属也。但与大怒血逆者不同，而治法亦有所异。盖此因欲火上炎，故血随气上，必其情欲动极而欲不能遂者有之，或借曲蘗以强遏郁火者亦有之。其证则忽而暴吐，或鼻衄不能禁止，或厥逆，或汗出，或气喘，或咳嗽，此皆以阴火上冲而然。凡治此者，必先制火以抑其势，清满化饮，四阴煎或加减一阴煎之类主之。其有阴竭于下，火不归源，别无烦热脉证，而血厥不止垂危者，非镇阴煎必不能救，待其势定，然后因证酌治之。[93p]

    For those treating this condition, one should primarily focus on nourishing and supporting the Mingmen (life gate), whether using water or fire, and the treatment should be based on methods for addressing the "non-wind gate."

    Moreover, the movement of blood characterized by color changes occurs because both blood and qi rush upward, which is also categorized as blood congestion. However, this is different from blood reversing due to intense anger, and thus, the treatment methods also vary. This condition often arises from the upward blazing of the desire fire, causing the blood to follow the qi upward. It typically involves strong emotional disturbances and the inability to express desires, and sometimes it involves using curative herbs to strongly suppress the excessive fire.

    Symptoms may include sudden and violent vomiting, nosebleeds that cannot be controlled, cold reversals, sweating, shortness of breath, or coughing—all of which result from the upward surge of yin fire.

    In treating this, one must first suppress the fire to control its momentum, clear the fullness, and transform excessive dampness, primarily using Four Yin Decoction or modified versions of similar prescriptions. If there is depletion of yin below and fire does not return to its source, with no other troubling heat pulse signs, and continuous blood congestion leading to a critical state, it is essential to use Zhen Yin Decoction, as it alone can provide rescue. Once the condition stabilizes, one can then adjust treatment according to the specific symptoms.[93p]

    　　　　　阴阳二厥

    　　厥有二证，阳厥阴厥也。阳厥者，热厥也，必其先自三阳传入阴分，故其初起必因头疼发热，自浅入深，然后及于三阴，变为四肢逆冷，或时乍温。其证必便结躁烦，谵语发渴，不恶寒反恶热，脉沉有力。此以传经热证所化，外虽手足厥冷，内则因于热邪。阳证发厥，故为阳厥，乃阳极似阴也。其证由邪热内结，或伏阳失下之所致也。凡厥微则热亦微，宜四逆散之类；厥甚则热亦甚，宜承气汤之类也。阴厥者，寒厥也，初无三阳传经实热等证，而真寒直入三阴，则畏寒厥冷，腹痛吐泻，战栗不渴，脉沉无力。此独阴无阳也，故为阴厥，轻则理中汤，重则四逆、回阳等汤主之。　　按阳厥阴厥，其辨如前，此先哲之大法也。然愚则有所辨。[94p]

    Yin and Yang Syndromes

    There are two types of syndromes: Yang syndrome and Yin syndrome. Yang syndrome, or heat syndrome, occurs when heat travels from the three Yang channels into the Yin system. It initially manifests as headache and fever, starting shallow and progressing deeper, eventually affecting the three Yin channels, leading to coldness in the limbs and sometimes warmth. The symptoms include constipation, restlessness, delirium, thirst, aversion to heat rather than cold, and a deep, strong pulse. This is caused by the transformation of heat in the channels; externally, the hands and feet may feel cold, but internally it is due to a pathogenic heat. When Yang syndrome manifests, it resembles Yin, hence it is called Yang syndrome. The symptoms arise from internal heat or loss of Yang at its descending point. If the syndrome is mild, the heat is also mild, and remedies like Si Ni San are appropriate; if severe, then stronger remedies like Cheng Qi Decoction are needed.

    Yin syndrome, or cold syndrome, does not initially show signs of heat from the three Yang channels. Instead, true cold directly invades the three Yin channels, causing aversion to cold, abdominal pain, vomiting, diarrhea, shivering, and a lack of thirst, with a deep, weak pulse. This syndrome is characterized by the absence of Yang, thus it is called Yin syndrome. For mild cases, Li Zhong Decoction is suitable, while for severe cases, Si Ni Decoction or Hui Yang Decoction are recommended.

    Note that the differentiation between Yang and Yin syndromes is as described; this is a fundamental principle of the ancients. However, I humbly offer my distinctions.[94p]

    如阴厥一证，既无阳证阳脉而病寒若此，明是阴证，今人但曰中寒者，即其病也。然犯此者无几，知此者无难，治宜温中，无待辨也。惟是阳厥一证，则有不得不辨者。夫厥由三阳所传，是为阳厥，此固然矣。即以传经者言之，又岂尽无阴证乎？故凡病真阳不足者，即阳中之阴厥也；脉弱无神者，即阳中之阴厥也；攻伐清凉太过者，即阳中之阴厥也。四肢为诸阳之本，使非有热结烦渴胀实等证，而见厥逆者，皆由阳气不足也。成无己曰：大抵厥逆为阴，所主寒者多矣。又曰：厥为阴之盛也。故凡属挟虚伤寒，则虽自阳经传入者，是亦阳中之阴厥也。阴中之阴者宜温，阳中之阴者果宜凉乎？学者勿谓先有头痛发热，但自三阳传至者，便为阳厥而寒因热用之，则为害不小矣。[95p]

    In cases of Yin inversion, where there are no Yang symptoms or Yang pulse but the illness manifests as cold, it is clearly a Yin condition. Nowadays, people simply call it middle cold, which is indeed the disease. However, few fall into this error, and it's not difficult to understand. The treatment should be to warm the center without needing further distinction.

    As for Yang inversion, distinguishing it is necessary. Inversion arises from the transmission of the three Yangs, leading to Yang inversion, which is indeed the case. Even in discussing transmission through the channels, can it be said that there are no Yin conditions? Therefore, any illness resulting from true Yang deficiency is also a Yin inversion within Yang; a weak pulse with no spirit is also a Yin inversion within Yang; excessive attack or cooling leads to a Yin inversion within Yang as well.

    The four limbs are the roots of all Yang; unless there are symptoms like heat accumulation, restlessness, thirst, or fullness, inverted coldness indicates a deficiency of Yang energy. Cheng Wujie stated: generally, inversion is related to Yin, and is often associated with coldness. He also said: inversion is the amplification of Yin. Therefore, conditions of combined deficiency and coldness, although they may arise from the Yang channels, are still a Yin inversion within Yang.

    Should Yin within Yin be warmed, or should Yin within Yang be cooled? Scholars should not think that the presence of headache and fever, merely due to the transmission of the three Yangs, automatically classifies it as Yang inversion, as treating cold caused by heat would lead to significant harm.[95p]

    　　　　　蛔厥

    　　成无己曰：脏厥者死，阳气绝也。蛔厥虽厥而烦，吐蛔已则静，不若脏厥而躁，无暂安时也。病人脏寒胃虚，故宜与乌梅丸，温脏安虫。然脏厥蛔厥二证，皆伤寒证也，详见伤寒门。[96p]

    Hui Jue (Intestinal Twists)

    Cheng Wujiy stated: "Zang Jue (Organ Collapse) leads to death, as the yang energy is severed. Although Hui Jue involves convulsions and distress, once the gut contents are expelled, the person will calm down. However, this is not preferable to Zang Jue, which is accompanied by restlessness, with no moment of peace. The patient suffers from cold organs and a weak stomach, thus it is advisable to administer Wumei Wan to warm the organs and stabilize the worms. Both Zang Jue and Hui Jue are related to febrile diseases, as detailed in the section on Febrile Diseases."[96p]

    　　　　石室秘箓 【清　陈士铎】

    　　　　　厥

    　　偏治法。如厥病一时手足厥逆，痛不可忍，人以为手足四肢之风证也，不知乃心中热蒸，外不能泄，故四肢手足则寒，而胸腹皮热如火。方用柴胡三钱，当归二钱、荆芥一钱，黄连二钱，炒栀子二钱，半夏一钱，枳壳一钱，水煎服，一剂即平，二剂即全愈。盖厥证多是火病，厥之甚则热之甚也，故舒其内热而四肢手足自温矣。方中妙在用柴胡为君，用诸寒凉之药，直入心肝之内，又不凝滞于胸膈之间。盖柴胡能散半表半里之邪，又善疏泄郁闷之气，若止治其四肢手足之风，而不直捣其中坚，则贼首不擒，余党安息？故不治四肢手足，而专治其心胸也。　　厥证虽多是火，然亦有非火而亦厥者，乃直中阴经也。阴寒直入于肾宫，则必挟肾水上犯心君之火，君弱臣强，犯上自所不免，若不用大热之药急救心君，则危亡顷刻。[97p]

    Secret Record of the Stone Chamber
    By Qing Dynasty Chen Shiduo

    The treatment method for the condition involves understanding that when one experiences sudden coldness and pain in the limbs, it is often mistaken for a wind-related issue of the extremities. In reality, it is the internal heat of the heart that cannot be released, leading to cold limbs while the chest and abdomen feel hot. The prescription consists of three qian of Chai Hu, two qian of Dang Gui, one qian of Jing Jie, two qian of Huang Lian, two qian of stir-fried Zhi Zi, one qian of Ban Xia, and one qian of Zhi Ke, which should be decocted in water. One dose will stabilize the condition, while two doses will lead to complete recovery. This is because many cases of cold limbs are due to internal fire, and intense coldness corresponds to intense heat. Thus, by relieving internal heat, the limbs will warm up. The brilliance of this formula lies in using Chai Hu as the chief ingredient, which, along with other cooling herbs, directly enters the heart and liver without causing stagnation in the chest. Chai Hu is adept at dispersing external and internal evils, and is effective in alleviating pent-up energy. Merely treating the limbs without addressing the core issue would be like capturing the underlings without catching the leader; the remaining forces would remain uncontained. Therefore, the focus should not be solely on the limbs but primarily on the heart and chest.

    While many cases of this condition are indeed caused by internal heat, there are also instances of coldness that lead to the same symptoms, resulting from chilled Yin entering the kidney palace. This will inevitably challenge the heart's fire with the kidney's cold water being on the rise, leading to a weakened ruling fire while the subordinate becomes strong. If one does not urgently use strong heating remedies to save the heart, a crisis could ensue at any moment.[97p]

    方用人参三钱，白朮一两，附子、肉桂、吴茱萸各一钱，水煎服，一剂即愈。然寒厥与热厥，大相悬绝，不可不辨。寒厥，手足必青，饮水必吐，腹必痛，喜火熨之。若热厥，手足虽寒而不青紫，饮水不吐，熨火则腹必加疼是也。能辨证清而用药当，下喉即定，便是神医，何必用追魂之符箓哉？　　开治法。如尸厥乃中邪气闭，必须用药以开之，不用瓜蒂散以探吐，即用皂角以取嚏也。方用瓜蒂七个，水二碗，煎汤一碗，加盐少许灌之，即大吐浓痰数碗而愈。或用皂角刺碾为细末，取鹅翎管盛药末，吹入病人鼻中，得打喷嚏，口吐浓痰如黄物者，即愈。盖厥证多系热邪，然热邪必然叫号，今黯然无语，宛似死人，明系阴虚之人，忽中阴邪，不可以治阳厥之法治之而至不救，不若先以瓜蒂、皂角取吐，以去其痰涎，声出后，以人参五钱，白薇一钱，茯苓三钱，白朮五钱，半夏二钱，治之自安。[98p]

    To treat, use three qian of ginseng, one liang of white atractylodes, one qian each of aconite, cinnamon, and evodia. Boil with water and take as a decoction; one dose will cure. However, it is crucial to distinguish between cold and heat patterns, as they are vastly different. In cold qi deficiency, the hands and feet will be blue, drinking water will induce vomiting, and there will be abdominal pain, with a preference for warmth for relief. In contrast, with heat qi deficiency, the hands and feet may feel cold but will not appear bluish; water will not induce vomiting, and warmth will exacerbate abdominal pain. If one can accurately diagnose and appropriately use medicine, the treatment will be effective as soon as it reaches the throat—this is the mark of a true healer, and there is no need for talismans or incantations.

    For treatment, if it is a case of corpse pattern due to evil qi blockage, medication must be used to open it. Do not use the gourd stem powder to induce vomiting; instead, use soapberry to provoke sneezing. Use seven gourd stems, and prepare with two bowls of water, reducing it to one bowl of decoction, adding a little salt to administer, which will induce a heavy cough with thick phlegm, resulting in cure. Alternatively, grind soapberry spines into fine powder, fill a goose feather quill with the powder, and blow it into the patient's nose. If they sneeze and expel thick phlegm resembling yellow substances, they will be cured. Most cases of qi deficiency are due to heat evil, yet the heat evil must manifest in cries; now, silently and lifelessly, resembling a corpse, it is clear this is a case of yin deficiency suddenly struck by yin evil. Therefore, do not treat a yang deficiency with methods meant for it, as this could lead to failure. It is better to first use gourd stem and soapberry to induce vomiting to remove phlegm. Once the voice returns, treat with five qian of ginseng, one qian of white peony, three qian of poria, five qian of white atractylodes, and two qian of pinellia to restore stability.[98p]

    此乃开治之一法也。　　喷嚏之法，用生半夏三钱为末，水丸如黄豆大，入鼻孔中，则必喷嚏不已，用水饮之立止。通治中风不语尸厥等证，中恶中鬼俱妙，皆开治之法也。　　引治法。如人病厥逆之证，不敢用药以治之，用吴茱萸一两为末，以面半两，水调成厚糊一般，以布如锺大，摊成膏纸，厚半分，贴在涌泉穴内，则手足不逆矣。况上热下寒之证，皆可用此法而治之，亦引火归元之法也。　　立治者，不可坐卧而立治之也。如厥证多两手反张，两足转逆，必须立而饮药，则顷刻立定。盖厥证原是热病，热深则厥亦深，倘令其卧而服药，则药到胃，一遇火气沸腾，冲击而不相入，反致吐出也。今立而饮药，则断断无吐出之虞。方用黄连、茯苓、白芍各三钱，柴胡、白芥子、木瓜、甘草各一钱，水煎服。[99p]

    This is indeed a method for opening treatment. The method for inducing sneezing is to grind three qian of fresh Pinellia into a powder, form it into water balls the size of yellow beans, and insert them into the nostrils; it will surely induce persistent sneezing. Drink water, and it will stop immediately. This method treats conditions like wind stroke, speechlessness, and corpse-like stupor, as well as demonic possession; all are excellent methods for opening treatment.

    The method of guiding treatment is as follows: if someone suffers from symptoms of reversal due to a stroke and is afraid to use medicine for treatment, take one liang of Wu zhu yu and grind it into a powder, mix it with half a liang of flour, and add water to form a thick paste. Spread it onto a cloth about the size of a bell, forming a thick paper about half a fen thick, and apply it to the Yongquan acupoint. This will keep the hands and feet from reversing. This method can also be used to treat symptoms of upper heat and lower cold; it is a method for guiding fire back to its source as well.

    For immediate treatment, one must not lie down or sit while administering the treatment. In cases where there is often reversal of the hands and feet, it is essential to stand and take the medicine, as it will stabilize instantly. This is because the symptoms of reversal originally stem from a heat disease; the deeper the heat, the more profound the reversal. If one lies down while taking the medicine, the medicine reaches the stomach, and upon encountering boiling fire qi, it will surge and not be absorbed, leading to vomiting. However, if one stands while taking the medicine, there will be no worry of vomiting. The prescription includes three qian each of Huang lian, Fu ling, and Bai shao, and one qian each of Chai hu, Bai jie zi, Mu guo, and Gan cao, to be boiled and taken.[99p]

    此方纯是平肝之品，去火而又顺火之性，自宜入口不吐。然而火热炎上，吐亦常有。令人将病人抱而立之，令一人将药与饮，俟其下口久之，然后抱卧，则药相顺而无吐逆之苦矣。　　人有忽然发厥，口不能言，眼闭手撒，喉中作酣声，痰气甚盛，有一日即死者，有二三日而死者，此厥多犯神明，然亦因素有痰气而发也。治法自宜攻痰为要，然徒攻痰而不开心窍，亦是徒然。方用启迷丹，生半夏、人参各五钱，菟丝子一两，甘草三分，茯神三钱，皂角荚、生姜各一钱，菖蒲二钱，水煎服。此方人参、半夏各用五钱，使攻补兼施，则痰易消而气易复。尤妙用菟丝子为君，则正气生而邪气散；更妙用皂荚、菖蒲、茯神开心窍以清心，自然气回而厥定。倘疑厥证是热，而轻用寒凉之药，则去生远矣。半夏用生不用制者，取其生气以救死，且制之过熟，反掣肘效迟，而不能奏功也。古今图书集成医部全录卷二百九十四[100p]

    This formula is purely for calming the liver, eliminating heat while also harmonizing the nature of heat, making it suitable for ingestion without causing any regurgitation. However, when heat rises, vomiting can often occur. Patients should be held upright, and one person should administer the medicine and drink, allowing it to stay in the mouth for a while before laying them down, so that the medicine can act smoothly without the distress of vomiting.

    Some individuals may suddenly faint, unable to speak, with closed eyes and limp hands, making snoring sounds from their throats, with excessive phlegm and gas, leading to death within a day for some, or two or three days for others. This condition often troubles the spirit, but it is also due to excessive phlegm and gas. The treatment should thus focus primarily on eliminating phlegm, but simply attacking phlegm without opening the orifices is futile. The formula used is the Qiming Pill: five qian each of fresh Pinellia and ginseng, one liang of dodder seed, three fen of licorice, three qian of Poria, one qian each of soap pod and fresh ginger, and two qian of sweet flag, to be decocted in water and taken.

    In this formula, both ginseng and Pinellia are used in equal amounts to provide both attacking and tonifying effects, making it easier to dissipate phlegm and restore qi. The use of dodder seed as the chief ingredient helps to restore vital energy and disperse pathogenic factors; the addition of soap pod, sweet flag, and Poria opens the orifices to clear the heart, naturally allowing the qi to return and the fainting to stabilize. If there are doubts about the fainting being due to heat, and cold medicines are lightly used, it will drive the vital energy away. Fresh Pinellia is used rather than processed to preserve its life force for rescue during critical moments; over-preparation leads to reduced efficacy, making it ineffective.[100p]

    厥门

    　　　　方

    　　茯苓甘草汤 【仲景，下同】 　伤寒厥而心下悸者，有水也，此治之。　　茯苓　桂枝各二两　生姜切，三两　甘草炙，一两　　右四味，以水四升，煮取二升，去滓，分温三服。

    　　通脉四逆加猪胆汁汤　治吐已下断汗出而厥，四肢拘急不解，脉微欲绝。　　即四逆汤方中，加入猪胆汁半合，余依前法服。[101p]

    Jue Men

    Fang

    Fu Ling and Gan Cao Decoction [Zhong Jing, same below] For those with cold extremities and palpitation beneath the heart due to water retention, this is the treatment.
    Ingredients: 2 taels of Fu Ling, 2 taels of Gui Zhi, 3 taels of fresh ginger (sliced), and 1 tael of roasted Gan Cao.
    Combine these four ingredients with 4 sheng of water, boil down to 2 sheng, strain, and divide into three warm doses.

    Si Ni Decoction For treating mismanaged sweating in the Taiyang stage, accompanied by cold extremities and needling sensations.
    Ingredients: 1.5 taels of dried ginger, 1 piece of Fu Zi (fresh, skins removed, broken into 8 pieces), and 2 taels of roasted Gan Cao.
    Crush these three ingredients and add to 3 sheng of water, boil down to 1 sheng and 2 ge, strain, and divide into three warm doses. A strong person may use 1 piece of Fu Zi and 3 taels of dried ginger taken cold.

    Tong Mai Si Ni Decoction with Pig Gallbladder Juice For those with vomiting, followed by sudden cessation of sweating, accompanied by cold extremities, stiffness of the limbs, and weak pulse nearing collapse.
    This is based on the Si Ni decoction formula, adding half a sheng of pig gallbladder juice, and following the previous method for administration.[101p]

    　　甘草干姜汤　治太阳内真寒而外假热，因误汗致厥者。　　甘草炙，四两　干姜炮，二两
    　　右(口父)咀，以水三升，煮取一升五合，去滓，分温再服。

    Licorice and Ginger Decoction: For treating true cold inside and false heat outside, caused by misguided sweating leading to collapse.
    Ingredients: Licorice (prepared) - 4 taels, Dry Ginger (stir-fried) - 2 taels.
    Preparation: Grind the above ingredients, use 3 sheng of water, boil until reduced to 1.5 sheng, strain, and take warm in two doses.

    White Tiger Decoction: For treating interior heat due to a cold injury, with a slippery pulse and collapse.
    Ingredients: Zhimu - 6 taels, Gypsum (crushed) - 1 pound, Licorice - 2 taels, Glutinous Rice - 6 taels.
    Preparation: Boil these four ingredients with 10 sheng of water until cooked, strain, and take 1 sheng warm, three times a day.

    Black Plum Pills: For treating worm-induced collapse and vomiting of worms.
    Ingredients: Black Plum - 300 pieces, Dry Ginger - 10 taels, Yellow Bitter - 1 pound, Fuzi (stir-fried), Cinnamon Twig, Ginseng, Huangbo, each 6 taels, Angelica, Xixin, Sichuan Pepper (seeds removed) - each 4 taels.
    Preparation: Individually grind and sift the ten ingredients, then soak the black plums in bitter wine overnight, remove the pits, and steam them. Mix with 5 sheng of cooked rice to make a paste, adding honey in a mortar, pound 200 times into pills the size of apricot kernels. Take 10 pills before meals, three times a day, gradually increasing to 20 pills. Avoid raw, cold, slippery foods and foul-tasting items.

    Angelica and Four Reversal Decoction: For treating cold collapse in hands and feet, with a weak pulse about to stop.
    Ingredients: Angelica - 3 taels, Cinnamon Twig - 3 taels, Peony - 3 taels, Xixin - 2 taels, Licorice (prepared) - 2 taels, Tongcao - 2 taels, Da Zao (jujube) - 35 pieces, split.
    Preparation: Boil these seven ingredients with 8 sheng of water until reduced to 3 sheng, strain, and take 1 sheng warm, three times a day.[102p]

    　　当归四逆加吴茱萸生姜汤　治前证内有久寒者。　　当归　桂枝　芍药各三两　甘草炙　通草　细辛各二两　生姜切，半斤　大枣三十五枚，擘　吴茱萸一升　　右九味，以水六升，清酒六升和煮，取五升，去滓，分温五服。一方水酒各四升。

    　　四逆散　治少阴病四逆，其人或咳或悸，或小便不利，或腹中痛，或泄利下重者，此主之。　　甘草炙　柴胡　枳实去白穰炒黄　芍药各一两　　右捣筛为细散，米饮调下二钱，日三服。[103p]

    Tang Gui Si Ni Jia Wu Zhu Yu Sheng Jiang Tang treats those with longstanding internal cold. The ingredients are:

    • Tang Gui (Angelica)
    • Gui Zhi (Cinnamon Twig)
    • Shao Yao (Peony Root), each three taels
    • Gan Cao (Licorice), charred
    • Tong Cao (Tea Plant)
    • Xi Xin (Asarum), each two taels
    • Fresh ginger, half a jin
    • Da Zao (Jujube), thirty-five pieces, split
    • Wu Zhu Yu (Evodia), one sheng

    Mix these nine ingredients with six sheng of water and six sheng of clear wine, boil down to five sheng, strain, and divide into five doses.

    Li Zhong Wan, prepared as decoction, is called Li Zhong Tang. It treats cold extremities, with a pulse that is deep, weak, and not rapid. Ingredients include:

    • Gan Jiang (Dried Ginger), roasted
    • Gan Cao, charred
    • Ren Shen (Ginseng), doubled for abdominal pain
    • Bai Zhu (Atractylodes), each one tael

    Crush and sift, mix with honey to form pills the size of egg yolks. For those with abdominal heat, take one pill crushed and mixed with hot water twice daily. If no heat is perceived, take three to four pills. It is advisable to eat warm gruel, cover slightly, and do not uncover clothing.

    Si Ni San treats lesser yin disorders with cold extremities, where individuals may cough, experience palpitations, face difficulty in urination, abdominal pain, or diarrhea. The treatment consists of:

    • Gan Cao, charred
    • Chai Hu (Bupleurum)
    • Zhi Shi (Bitter Orange), white pulp removed, toasted yellow
    • Shao Yao, each one tael

    Crush and sift into a fine powder, and mix two qian with rice drink, taken three times daily.[103p]

    　　白通加猪胆汁汤　治少阴病下利脉微者，与白通汤利不止厥逆无脉干呕烦者，白通加猪胆汁汤主之。服汤脉暴出者死，微续者生。　　猪胆半合　干姜炮，五钱　附子生去皮，半个　葱白四茎　溺二合半　　右以水一盏，煎五分，去滓内尿、胆汁，和相得，分温再服。
    　　大柴胡汤　治阳厥。
    　　柴胡半斤　黄芩　芍药各三两　生姜切，五两　半夏洗，半升　枳实炙，四枚　大枣十二枚，擘　　右七味，以水一斗二升，煮取六升，去滓再煎，温服一升，日三服。一方用大黄二两。若不加大黄，恐不为大柴胡也。
    　　桂枝麻黄各半汤　治寒热而厥，两手无脉，或一手无脉，用绵衣包手者。　　桂枝二两十六铢　芍药　生姜切　甘草炙　麻黄各一两　杏仁去皮尖及两仁者，二十四个　大枣四枚，擘　　右七味，以水五升，先煮麻黄一二沸，去上沫，内诸药中，煮取一升八合，去滓，温服六合。[104p]

    Baitong plus Pig Gallbladder Soup: Treats lesser yin disease with diarrhea and weak pulse. For those with continuous diarrhea and reversed qi with no pulse, and with dry heaving and anxiety, the Baitong plus Pig Gallbladder Soup is the main remedy. If upon taking the soup the pulse emerges violently, it indicates death; if the pulse slightly continues, there is hope for life.

    Ingredients:

    • Half a pig gallbladder
    • Dried ginger, roasted, 5 qian
    • Fresh aconite, peeled, half a piece
    • Four green onion stalks
    • Urine, 2.5 sheng

    Boil in one cup of water until reduced to a fifth, remove the dregs, mix with urine and gallbladder, and take warm in divided doses.

    Major Chai Hu Decoction: Treats yang collapse.

    Ingredients:

    • Chai Hu, 1 jin
    • Huang Qin, 3 liang
    • Shao Yao, 3 liang
    • Fresh ginger, sliced, 5 liang
    • Ban Xia, washed, half sheng
    • Zhi Shi, roasted, 4 pieces
    • Da Zao, 12 pieces, split

    Combine these seven ingredients with 12 sheng of water, boil down to 6 sheng, remove dregs, and re-boil. Take 1 sheng warm, thrice daily. One variation uses 2 liang of Da Huang. If Da Huang is not added, it may not be considered Major Chai Hu.

    Gui Zhi and Ma Huang Half Decoction: Treats cold-heat and collapse, with no pulse in either hand, or one hand without pulse, when wrapped in a cotton garment.

    Ingredients:

    • Gui Zhi, 2 liang 26 qian
    • Shao Yao
    • Fresh ginger, sliced
    • Gan Cao, roasted
    • Ma Huang, each 1 liang
    • Apricot kernels, peeled and pointed, 24 pieces
    • Da Zao, 4 pieces, split

    Combine these seven ingredients with 5 sheng of water. First boil Ma Huang until bubbling, remove foam, then add the other herbs, boil down to 1 sheng 8 jiao, remove dregs, and take warm in 6 parts.[104p]

    　　右为细末，每服三钱，蜜少许，温水调下，或无蜜亦可，每日三服。或欲冷饮者，新井泉调下亦得。解利发汗，煎葱白豆豉汤下，每服水一盏。葱白五寸，豆豉五十粒，煮取汁七分调，并三四服，以效为度。此药是寒凉解散热郁，设病甚不解，多服无害，但有益耳。一名天水散，一名太白散，一名六一散。[105p]

    Ephedra Decoction treats the cold inversion of the three Yin. Use two taels of ephedra (remove the nodes), two taels of honey-fried licorice, and one piece of prepared aconite (remove the skin). Combine these three ingredients with seven sheng of water. First, boil the ephedra for one or two boils, skim off the froth, add the other herbs, and boil down to three sheng. Strain and take one sheng warm.

    Yiyuan Powder (according to He Jian) combines to treat profound heat inversion with a strong pulse. Use six taels of good white talc and one tael of licorice. Grind these into a fine powder. Take three qian each time, mix with a little honey, and take with warm water. If there is no honey, you may omit it, taking three doses daily. For those who prefer cool drinks, it can also be mixed with fresh spring water. It helps alleviate heat and induces sweating; taking it with a decoction of scallion whites and fermented broad beans, using one cup of water each time. Use five inches of scallion whites and fifty grains of fermented broad beans, boil to extract seven portions of juice, and take in three or four doses as needed. This medicine cools down and disperses trapped heat; if the illness is severe and does not resolve, taking more poses no harm but is beneficial. It is also known as Tian Shui Powder, Tai Bai Powder, and Liu Yi Powder.[105p]

    　　黄连解毒汤　治热厥下后，热少退而未愈者。　　黄连　黄蘗　黄芩　大栀子各五钱
    　　右銼如麻豆大，每服称五钱，水一茶盏，煎至四分，绞取汁，温服无时，日三四，以效为度，每一二服效。或腹满呕吐，或欲作利者，每服加半夏三枚全用，厚朴二钱銼，茯苓去皮銼，水一盏半，生姜三片，煎至半盏，　　绞汁温服，名曰半夏黄连解毒汤。或欲急下者，本方加大承气汤一服，生姜煎，如前法，以利为度；一法为细末，水和如小豆大，温水下二十丸，治积热劳咳泻利，甚良。

    Huanglian Jiedu Decoction treats heat-induced syncope after defecation, where the heat has lessened but not yet resolved. The ingredients are: Huanglian, Huangbai, Huangsine, and Dazhi Zi, each five qian.

    Grind them to the size of a broad bean. For each dose, weigh five qian, add one teacup of water, and simmer until reduced to one-fourth the original volume. Strain the juice and take it warm at any time, three to four times a day, adjusting as needed; it may take one or two doses to see results. If there is abdominal fullness or vomiting, or if one needs to defecate, add three pieces of Banxia (Pinellia ternata) completely used, two qian of Houpo (Magnolia bark) ground, peeled Fuling (Poria) ground, with one and a half teacups of water, and three slices of fresh ginger, simmer until half a teacup remains, strain the juice and take it warm. This is called Banxia Huanglian Jiedu Decoction. For urgent defecation, add one dose of Dachengqi Decoction to the original formula, simmer with ginger as before, adjusting for laxation; an alternative is to make into fine powder, mix with water to the size of a small bean, take twenty pills with warm water, effective for heat accumulation leading to cough, diarrhea, and is quite beneficial.

    Shuangjie Powder: Treats syncope combined with internal and external evils. Ingredients are: Yiyuan Powder and Fangfeng Tongsheng Powder, each seven liang.

    Mix the two ingredients thoroughly in one place. For each dose, take three qian, with one and a half teacups of water, add five inches of scallion white, fifty grains of salted fermented soybeans, and three slices of fresh ginger, simmer until only one teacup remains, and take it warm.[106p]

    Eight-Flavored Qi-Regulating Powder by Danxi
    For treating Qi collapse.
    Ingredients:

    • 1 liang of white atractylodes
    • 1 liang of white poria
    • 1 liang of orange peel
    • 1 liang of white angelica
    • 1 liang of tangerine peel

    • 1 liang of ginseng

    Take 5 qian each time, using 1.5 jings of water, decoct until reduced by a third, and take warm. Additionally, take with wine to dissolve the Suhexiang pill at intervals.

    Ginger and Aconite Decoction by Zhongjing
    For treating interior cold, strong rigidity of the body, inability to speak, and counter-cold.
    Ingredients:

    • 1 liang of dried ginger
    • 1 piece of processed aconite, with skin and navel removed

    Each dose is 3 qian, taken as a decoction.
    For condensed Qi causing stabbing pain, add 5 fen of nutmeg.
    For condensed Qi with numbness, add 1 qian of windbreak.
    For those with dampness, add white atractylodes.
    For tight tendons and muscles, add 1 portion of papaya.
    For pain in the limbs and joints, add 2 qian of cinnamon.

    Phlegm-Expelling Decoction
    For treating phlegm Qi counterflow.
    Procedure: Prepare nitrate in the same manner as radish, boil with water, remove the radish, filter until settled, and place in a cow gall bladder, let it dry in December, weighing 5 qian; or use only the dried nitrate. Alternatively, use 2 liang of green stone, crushed, with 2 liang of fiery nitrate, all placed in a small ceramic jar covered with a clay tile, tightly bound with iron wire, sealed with salt mud, dried in the sun, and then roasted until red, allowing it to cool and extracting the residue.

    This should be ground into powder, forming pills the size of a jujube; take 30 to 50 pills with warm water. Another method adds 5 qian of blue atractylodes and 1 liang of talcum, adjusting treatment based on the patient's cold, heat, deficiency, and excess.[107p]

    Adjusting Qi Powder: Taken with Ping Wei Powder to treat corpse qi syndromes.
    Ingredients: White cardamom, clove, sandalwood, and wood fragrance each 2 qian; huoxiang and honey-fried licorice each 8 qian; sand ginger 4 qian. Grind these into a powder. Take 2 qian per dose, mix with a little salt, and consume with boiling hot water.

    Ping Wei Powder: For treating symptoms, see the specification under Adjusting Qi Powder.
    Ingredients: Cang zhu soaked in 5 jin, thick bark (Houpo) and ginger-prepared fried each 3 jin; dried tangerine peel 3 jin; honey-fried licorice 30 liang. Grind this into a powder.     Si Qi Decoction: Treats phlegm and qi reversal.
    Ingredients: Thick bark 2 liang, poria 4 liang, half summer 5 liang, purple perilla 2 liang. For each dose, take 4 qian, combine with 1 zhong of water, 7 slices of ginger, and 1 date, and decoct.

    Returning Yang Emergency Decoction: Treats the onset of cold damage, without headache or body heat, manifesting as aversion to cold, cold limbs, or excessive cold at the elbows and knees, abdominal pain with vomiting or diarrhea, or foamy, cold saliva from the mouth, or shivering with a face as if scraped by a knife, curling up in bed without thirst, pulse being deep, slow, and weak indicates a true cold condition directly affecting the yin channel rather than transmitting from the yang channel.
    Ingredients: Ginseng, white atractylodes, poria, dried tangerine peel, half summer, dried ginger, cinnamon, aconite, schisandra, licorice. The ingredients are ground, prepared with 3 slices of fresh ginger, and decocted for consumption.[108p]

    　　熨法　治寒邪直入三阴，无头痛身热，恶寒腹痛，下利清白，唇青面黑，吐沫口噤，或身痛如被杖，四肢厥冷，上过乎肘，下过乎膝，引衣蜷卧，不渴，脉来沉迟无力，及一切虚寒，并能治之。　　葱细切　麦麸各三升　盐一斤
    　　右用水和匀，分作二处，炒令极热，重绢包之，乘热熨脐，冷更易一包。其葱包既冷，再用水拌炒热，依前用之。如大小便不通，亦用此法。
    　　三生饮 【《良方》，下同】 　治痰厥气厥。　　南星生用，五钱　木香一钱五分　川乌去皮　附子去皮，生用，各一钱　　右作一服，水二锺，生姜七片，煎至一锺，不拘时服。有卒中风不省人事者，以苏合香丸，用生姜自然汁化开擦牙。[109p]

    Method of Application: To treat cold evils that penetrate the three yin, with no headache, body heat, aversion to cold, abdominal pain, diarrhea with clear fluids, blue lips and a black face, foaming at the mouth and inability to speak, or body pain as if struck with a rod, limbs cold and stiff, upper body above the elbows, lower body below the knees, drawing clothing and curling up, with no thirst, pulse coming in with a沉 (deep) and迟 (slow) and powerless manner, and all forms of deficiency and cold can be treated.

    Ingredients:

    • Scallions, finely chopped: 3 sheng
    • Wheat bran: 3 sheng
    • Salt: 1 jin

    Mix with water evenly, divide into two portions, fry until very hot, and wrap in heavy cloth. While still hot, apply to the navel; when it cools, replace with another pack. When the scallion pack has cooled, fry again with water until hot and use as before. If there is difficulty with urination or defecation, use this method as well.

    San Sheng Drink (according to the "Good Recipe"): To treat phlegm and blood stasis.

    • Fresh Nux vomica: 5 qian
    • Wood scent: 1 qian 5 fen
    • Chuanwu (dried Aconitum): skinned, and
    • Fuzi (Aconiti radix): skinned and fresh, each: 1 qian

    Prepare this as one dose; add two sheng of water and seven slices of ginger, simmer until one sheng remains, and take without regard to time. For those who suddenly lose consciousness due to wind stroke, use Sihuoxiang pills, dissolve with natural juice of fresh ginger, and use to brush teeth.[109p]

    　　追魂汤　治卒厥暴死，及客忤、鬼击、蜚尸、奄忽气绝口噤。　　麻黄六钱　杏仁去皮尖，五十粒　甘草炙，二钱　　右，分作二服，煎至七分，去滓灌之，口噤斡开。若更不下，分病人发左右提搦肩引之，药下渐苏。若唇青身冷为入脏，即死；身和汗出即愈。《千金方》有桂。
    　　甘竹沥汤　治卒中恶，风噎倒闷，口噤不能语；肝厥尸厥，死不识人，闭目，灸针不知痛，风狂，宜服此汤。　　甘竹沥一斗　生姜　防风　甘草炙，各三两　防己　麻黄去节　人参　黄芩　白朮　细辛　茵芋　秦艽　桂心各一两　附子一枚，大者，炮　　右(口父)咀，以汤渍药令赤，合竹沥，煮取四升，分为四服。忌海藻、松菜、桃李、雀肉、生葱、生菜、猪肉、冷水。[110p]

    Soul-Rescue Decoction: Treats sudden death from exhaustion, and when a guest is startled, or if afflicted by a spirit, also treats sudden loss of breath leading to speechlessness.

    Ingredients:

    • Ephedra (6 qian)
    • Bitter almond (50, skin and tip removed)
    • Honey-fried licorice (2 qian)

    Prepare as follows: Divide into two doses, decoct to seven parts, remove dregs, and administer. If the patient remains speechless, gently pull at their shoulders and sides to help administer the medicine, gradually reviving them. If the lips turn blue and the body feels cold, it may indicate internal organ failure, leading to death; if the body warms and sweats, recovery is possible.

    From "Thousand Golden Prescriptions" it also mentions cinnamon.

    Sweet Bamboo Drain Decoction: Treats sudden sickness from a stroke, wind blocking the throat causing faintness, leading to inability to speak; also addresses liver or ghost-induced faintness, where the person does not recognize others, keeps eyes shut, and does not feel pain from needle moxibustion, experiencing wild wind symptoms; this decoction should be taken.

    Ingredients:

    • Sweet bamboo drain (1 dou)
    • Fresh ginger (3 liang)
    • Wind protection (3 liang)
    • Honey-fried licorice (3 liang)
    • Stephania (1 liang)
    • Ephedra, removed from stems (1 liang)
    • Ginseng (1 liang)
    • Scutellaria (1 liang)
    • Atractylodes (1 liang)
    • Asarum (1 liang)
    • Yam (1 liang)
    • Gentian (1 liang)
    • Cinnamon heart (1 liang)
    • Aconite (1 piece, preferably larger, processed)

    Preparation: Chew and combine the herbs with bamboo drain until red, boil to obtain four sheng, divide into four doses. Avoid consuming seaweed, pine greens, peach and plum, sparrow meat, raw green onions, raw lettuce, pork, and cold water.[110p]

    　　人参汤　治风厥志意不乐，身背疼痛，多惊，善欠噫气。　　人参　川芎　枳壳麸炒　芍药　防风　细辛　附子炮裂去皮脐　甘草炙　桂心各五钱　桔梗炒　茯神去木　木香各一分　　右(口父)咀，每服五钱匕，水一盏半，生姜半分，煎至八分，去滓温服。
    　　三建汤　治元阳素虚，寒邪外攻，手足厥冷，六脉沉微，大小便滑数。凡中风涎潮，不省人事，伤寒阴证，皆可服之。　　大川乌　附子　天雄俱炮去皮脐，各三钱　　右作一服，用水二锺，生姜十片，煎至一锺，不拘时服。自汗加肉桂、浮麦各一钱。气逆者，加沉香一钱。胃冷者，加丁香、胡椒各五分。[111p]

    Ginseng Soup: Used for treating wind-induced fainting, melancholy, body aches, frequent shocks, and good at relieving breathlessness. Ingredients: Ginseng, Chuanxiong, stir-fried Zhihua, Peony, Fangfeng, Xixin, prepared Fuzi with skin and navel removed, honey-fried Licorice, and Cinnamon Heart, each five qian; stir-fried Platycodon and prepared Fushen with wood removed, and Mu Xiang, each one fen. Grind the ingredients and take five qian worth each time, using one and a half bowls of water with half a fen of fresh ginger, decoct until reduced to eight parts, strain and take warm.

    San Jian Soup: Used for nourishing the original Yang that is fundamentally deficient, with cold evil attacking from the outside, leading to cold extremities, weak pulse, and frequent slippery bowel movements. It can be taken for cases of wind stroke with phlegm floods, unconsciousness, and manifestations of cold from febrile diseases. Ingredients: Daturae, Fuzi, and Tianxiong, each three qian. Prepare into one dose using two bowls of water and ten slices of fresh ginger, decoct until reduced to one bowl, and can be taken at any time. For spontaneous sweating, add one qian of cinnamon and floating wheat each. If there is breath reversal, add one qian of sandalwood. If there is cold in the stomach, add half a fen each of clove and pepper.[111p]

    　　洞阳丹　治阳虚阴盛，手足厥冷，暴吐大下，脉细羸瘦，伤寒阴证，并皆治之。　　川乌四两　天雄并炮去皮，三两　锺乳粉　附子炮去皮脐，各二两　阳起石　朱砂研，各一两　　右为细末，酒煮神曲糊丸如梧桐子大，每服五十丸，空心，用温酒或盐汤送下。
    　　接真汤　治阴病，手足厥冷，脐腹疼痛，真气不足，衰惫欲绝。　　沉香　丁香各二钱　附子炮去皮脐，四钱　麝香一钱　　右銼碎，用水二锺，生姜七片，枣二枚去核，煎至七分，去滓，空心温服。
    　　四君子汤　治气虚厥逆。
    　　人参一钱　白朮　茯苓各二钱　甘草六分　　右，生姜三片，枣子一枚，水煎，不拘时温服。加半夏、陈皮，名六君子汤，治气虚痰厥。
    　　四物汤　治血虚厥逆。
    　　白芍药　当归　熟地　川芎各二钱[112p]

    Dongyang Dan treats yang deficiency with excess yin, cold extremities, sudden vomiting and severe diarrhea, thin and frail pulse, and injuries from cold.

    Ingredients:

    • 4 taels of Chuanwu
    • 3 taels of Tianxiong, both processed and peeled
    • 2 taels each of Zhongru powder and peeled Fuzi
    • 1 tael each of Yangqishi and ground cinnabar

    Grind these into a fine powder, and using wine, boil with shenqu to form pills the size of a paulownia seed. Take fifty pills at a time on an empty stomach, using warm wine or salty soup to wash down.

    Jiezhen Decoction treats yin diseases, cold extremities, abdominal pain, insufficient true qi, and exhaustion approaching death.

    Ingredients:

    • 2 qian each of sandalwood and clove
    • 4 qian of peeled Fuzi
    • 1 qian of musk

    Crush these and use 2 zhong of water, along with 7 slices of ginger and 2 pitted dates. Boil down to seven tenths, strain, and take warm on an empty stomach.

    Si Junzi Decoction treats qi deficiency with counterflow.

    Ingredients:

    • 1 qian of ginseng
    • 2 qian each of white atractylodes and poria
    • 6 fen of licorice

    Combine with 3 slices of ginger and 1 date; boil in water and take warm at any time. Adding Banxia and Chenpi yields the Liu Junzi Decoction, which treats qi deficiency with phlegm and counterflow.

    Si Wu Decoction treats blood deficiency with counterflow.

    Ingredients:

    • 2 qian each of white peony, angelica, cooked earth, and chuanxiong.[112p]

    　　右，水煎温服。

    　　木香匀气散　一名木香调气散。治气滞厥逆。　　木香　丁香　白檀香　白豆蔻　藿香叶　甘草各八钱　砂仁四钱　　右为末，每二钱，入盐少许，沸汤点服。一方有沉香。

    Take the above preparation warm with water.

    Muxiang Yunqi San, also known as Muxiang Tiaoqi San, treats stagnant qi and counterflow. The ingredients include: Muxiang, Dingxiang, Bai Danxiang, Bai Doukou, Huoxiang leaf, and Gancao, each 8 qian; Sharen 4 qian. Grind them into a powder, take 2 qian each time, add a small amount of salt, and take with boiling water. One version includes Chenxiang.

    Bajian Shunqi San treats sudden counterflow with a chilly body.

    Si Junzi Decoction with Qingpi, Chenpi, Bai Zhi, and Wu Yao in equal parts; prepare with ginger. Also take Suhexiang Wan combined with wine, which is excellent.

    Suhexiang Wan treats symptoms mentioned earlier. It addresses all sudden phlegm obstruction and counterflow. The ingredients are: Baizhu, Qingmuxiang, Zhushā, Xijiao, Chenxiang, Shexiang, Hezi peel, Dingxiang, Anxi Xiang, Bichengsu, and Bai Danxiang, each 2 liang; Longnao, Xunlu Xiang, and Suhexiang each 1 liang. Grind into a powder, using Anxi Xiang, and cook with wine to make a paste, mixing with fragrant oil and honey. For each dose, take a round ball the size of a tung seed, and take with well water, warm or cold as preferred, taking four balls. For the elderly and children, mix with wine for taking one ball.

    Liu Yu Decoction relieves all forms of stagnation and treats counterflow.

    Chenpi, Banxia, Chuanxiong, and Cangzhu each 1 qian; Chi Fuling and Zhizi each 7 fen; Xiangfu 2 qian; Sharen and Gancao each 5 fen. Boil with three slices of ginger and take warm, adjusting the dosages according to symptoms.[113p]

    Er Chen Decoction: Treats phlegm and convulsions.
    Ingredients: 2 qian of dried tangerine peel, 1 qian of pinellia, 8 fen of poria, 4 fen of licorice. Prepare with 3 slices of ginger, boil in water and take warm.

    Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction: Treats damp-heat stuck in the spleen, unable to nourish the limbs, leading to heat convulsions.
    Ingredients: 1 qian each of astragalus, ginseng, licorice; 5 fen each of angelica, white atractylodes, dried tangerine peel, bupleurum, and schizonepeta. For severe deficiency, increase bupleurum and schizonepeta to 1 fen each, and reduce for those with heavy sweating. Prepare with water, take warm just before noon. For severe cases, take two doses in succession. If there is slight sweating, it indicates recovery. Avoid excessive talking and labor; rest quietly for an hour or two before advancing to nourishing meals. For regular use, remove bupleurum and schizonepeta, and add 3 fen of phellodendron to nourish kidney water; 2 fen of safflower may nourish blood, but excessive use may damage blood.

    Huo Yu Decoction: Treats heat convulsions.
    Ingredients: 1 qian 5 fen each of cimicifuga, kudzu root, bupleurum, and white peony; 1 qian each of ledebouriella and licorice. Prepare with scallions and consume as a decoction.

    Dang Gui Long Hui Pills: For heat convulsions with phlegm obstructing the upper body and fire stagnation below, use the guiding phlegm decoction to swallow the Long Hui pills.
    Ingredients: 1 qian of costus, 1 liang each of angelica, gentian, gardenia, coptis, and scutellaria; 5 qian each of rhubarb, aloe, and indigo. Grind to a fine powder, add 5 fen of musk, and mix with honey to form small pills the size of red beans, taking with ginger decoction in doses of 39 every two or three times.[114p]

    　　沉香　乌药　枳实　槟榔
    　　右四味，以白汤共磨服。

    Four Grind Decoction: Treats various qi disorders and counterflow.
    Ingredients: Chenxiang (agarwood), Wuyao (lindera), Zhishi (sour orange), Binglang (betel nut).
    Mix these four ingredients with white soup and grind to take.

    Xingxiang Decoction: Treats phlegm and qi counterflow with body heat and facial redness. Recommended for consumption.
    Ingredients: Nanxing (dichroa root) 8 qian, Muxiang (saussurea) 1 qian.
    Prepare two doses with two zhongs of water, ten slices of ginger, and simmer until reduced by seven tenths, taking as needed.

    Chenxiang Gui Fu Pill: Treats deficiency and cold of the middle qi, cold extremities, inability to stretch the waist, and preference for gentle heat applications.
    Ingredients: Fuzi (prepared aconite) 1 liang (oz), Chuanwu (prepared black seed) 1 liang, Chenxiang (agarwood) 1 liang, Rougui (cinnamon) 1 liang, Ganjing (dried ginger) 1 liang, Liangjiang (galanga) 1 liang, Huixiang (fennel) 1 liang, Wuzhuyu (evodia) 1 liang.
    Grind to a powder and make into dough balls the size of tung seeds; take 50 to 70 pills before meals with rice drink, twice daily. Avoid raw and cold foods.

    Yangzheng Dan: Treats conditions of excess above and deficiency below with dizziness and counterflow. This medicine regulates the ascent and descent of yin and yang.
    Ingredients: Sulfur powder 1 liang, Black tin (lead) purified 1 liang, Mercury 1 liang, Cinnabar (red mercury sulfide) 1 liang.
    Melt the tin, add the sulfur powder gradually while stirring to form a fine powder. Add mercury and grind evenly; if hard, gently heat above the fire, then grind well and let cool. Make into very fine pills the size of chickpeas; take thirty pills with warm salt soup on an empty stomach.[115p]

    　　六味回阳饮 【《景岳全书》，下同】 　治手足厥逆，微阳将脱等证。　　人参一二两或数钱　炙甘草一钱　炮干姜　制附子各二三钱　当归身三钱，泄泻或动血者代以冬朮　熟地五钱或一两　　水二锺，武火煎七八分，温服。

    Liu Wei Hui Yang Decoction
    Used for treating hand and foot reversal of cold, signs of slight Yang exhaustion.

    • Ginseng: 1-2 liang or a few qian
    • Honey-fried licorice: 1 qian
    • Prepared dried ginger: 2-3 qian
    • Prepared aconite: 2-3 qian
    • Dong quai (main root): 3 qian (for diarrhea or blood movement, replace with winter worm)
    • Cooked rehmannia: 5 qian or 1 liang
    • Water: 2 zhong, boil over strong heat until 7-8 parts reduced, take warm.

    Zhen Yin Decoction
    Used for treating Yin deficiency below, contravening Yang above, signs of reversal.

    • Cooked rehmannia: 1-2 liang
    • Honey-fried licorice: 1 qian
    • Alisma: 1.5 qian
    • Cinnamon: 1-2 qian
    • Prepared aconite: 0.5-1.5 qian
    • Achyranthes: 2 qian
    • Water: 2 zhong, boil quickly and take.

    Si Wei Hui Yang Decoction
    Used for treating hand and foot reversal, original Yang deficiency, imminent danger.

    • Ginseng: 1-2 liang
    • Prepared aconite: 2-3 qian
    • Honey-fried licorice: 1-2 qian
    • Prepared dried ginger: 2-3 qian
    • Water: 2 zhong, boil over strong heat until 7-8 parts reduced, take warm, sip slowly.

    Tong Yu Decoction
    Used for treating blood stasis.

    • Hawthorn: 2 qian
    • Cyperus: 2 qian
    • Safflower (lightly roasted): 2 qian
    • Lindera: 1-2 qian

    • Orange peel: 1.5 qian
    • Wood fragrance: 0.7 qian
    • Water: 2 zhong, boil until 7 parts remain, add 1-2 small cups of wine, take before meals.[116p]

    Regulating Qi Powder
    For treating sudden syncope.
    White cardamom, clove, white sandalwood, wood fragrance, patchouli leaves, and honey-fried licorice, each eight qian; sand ginger four qian.
    Grind these into a fine powder. Take two qian each time, add a pinch of salt, and mix with boiling water to ingest.

    Schisandra Decoction
    Treats hidden Yin syncope, with cold extremities, a faint pulse on the verge of cessation, and symptoms of Qi deficiency.
    One ounce of schisandra, and five qian each of ginseng, ophiopogon, apricot kernel, and dried tangerine peel.
    Add one slice of ginger and one jujube, then decoct. This is the same as Shengmai San with the addition of dried tangerine peel and apricot kernel.

    Regulating Qi and Harmonizing the Stomach Powder
    For treating sudden unresponsive syncope due to invasion of pathogenic Qi, leading to loss of consciousness.
    White cardamom, clove, sandalwood, and wood fragrance each two qian; patchouli and sand ginger each four qian; licorice six qian.
    Grind these into a fine powder. Take two qian each time, add a pinch of salt, and mix with boiling water to ingest.

    Cangong Powder
    For treating blood syncope.
    Gourd stem, rhizoma of parched toad, calcined alum, and realgar in equal parts.
    Grind these into a fine powder. Use a small amount to blow into the nostrils to induce sneezing. This medicine can revive the dead.

    White Wei Decoction
    For the same indications as above.
    White wei and angelica each two qian; ginseng one and a half qian; honey-fried licorice seven fen.
    Add to half a cup of water and decoct until reduced to seven portions, then warm and ingest.[117p]

    Returning Soul Soup
    Treats blood reversal leading to sudden fainting, also for postpartum blood fainting and unconsciousness, eyes closed and mouth locked; this illness is mostly found in women.
    Ingredients: equal parts of angelica wine, ligusticum, cinnamon, dried ginger, processed, red peony, licorice, black beans (fried and husked), and perilla.
    Preparation: Boil in half a water cup; alternatively, grind to a fine powder, take two qian mixed with wine.

    Ginseng Solidifying Pills
    Treats fainting caused by heat.
    Ingredients: 2 liang of ginseng, and 4 liang each of asparagas, ophiopogon, raw earth, and cooked earth.
    Preparation: Grind into powder and make into pills for consumption.

    Puhuang Decoction
    Treats blood stagnation in the upper part, resulting in thin fainting.
    Ingredients: 1 liang of puhuang, toasted until brown;
    Mix with 10 jugs of clear wine, warm and consume.

    Ginseng Powder
    Treats heat-induced fainting, dizziness, inability to hear, unclear vision, and excessive anger.
    Ingredients: 2 liang each of ginseng, polygala, red poria, and fangfeng; and 1 liang each of peony, ophiopogon, dried tangerine peel (white part removed), and white atractylodes.
    Preparation: Grind to powder, take three qian with 1.5 water cups, boil until reduced to 80%, strain and consume warm.

    Red Poria Decoction
    Treats thin fainting and sudden anger, which can injure liver qi and cause disharmony in the chest, potentially leading to vomiting blood and nasal bleeding.
    Ingredients: 1 liang each of red poria, ginseng, platycodon, and dried tangerine peel; and 0.5 liang each of peony, ophiopogon, and betel nut.
    Preparation: Grind to powder, take three qian with 1 water cup, five slices of fresh ginger, boil until reduced to 80%, strain and consume warm.[118p]

    Yuan Zhi San
    Treats wind with many shocks, leading to back pain, good sighing, good yawning, a lack of joy in spirit, and body aches.

    Treats cold pain in the abdomen from qi stagnation, leading to cold in the lower body membranes.
    Ingredients: Wu Zhu Yu (2 taels, washed and fried), Chuan Wu (skinned and prepared), Xi Xin (each 3 taels), Liang Jiang, Dang Gui, Gan Jiang (prepared), Guan Gui (each 1 tael).
    Grind these to a powder. Take 2 qian with 1 cup of water, decoct until reduced to 70%, strain and take warm, three doses a day.

    Sheng Yang Xie Huo Tang (Dong Yuan)
    Treats qi deficiency with downward descent, leading to cold limbs.
    Ingredients: Qiang Huo, Huang Qi, Cang Zhu (soaked, skinned, and dried, each 1 tael), Gan Cao (roasted), Ren Shen, Huang Qin (each 7 qian), Chai Hu (1.5 taels), Huang Lian (prepared with wine, 0.5 taels), Sheng Ma (8 qian), Shi Gao (a small amount for summer).
    Grind these (to a coarse powder). Take 3 qian with 2 cups of water, decoct until reduced to 1 cup, strain, and take warm after breakfast and before lunch, every other day.[119p]

    If rigidity persists, and the pulse remains as before: Use stove soot to make pill size, mixed with broth and administered, while also needling the hundred meeting point and the side of the fingernail of the big toe on the foot. [from "Thousand Gold Formulas"][120p]

    　　痰厥气绝，心头尚温者：千年石灰一合，水一盏煎滚，去清水，再用一盏煎极滚，澄清灌之，少顷痰下自省。【《集元方》】
    　　热厥气痛：元明粉三钱，热童尿调下。 【《集简方》】

    　　热厥心痛，或发或止，久不愈，身热足寒者：元胡索去皮、金铃子肉等分为末，每温酒或白汤下二钱。【《圣惠方》】
    　　痰厥，头痛如破，厥气上冲，痰塞胸膈：炮附子三分，金墨四钱，冷水调服方寸匕，当吐即愈。忌猪肉冷水。

    • For phlegm collapse causing qi obstruction with warmth remaining in the heart: Mix one equal part of a thousand-year lime with one cup of water, boil it, remove the clear water, then boil again with another cup until it is completely clear, then administer it.     　　呕逆厥逆，内有寒痰：半夏一升，洗滑焙碾，小麦面一升，水和作弹丸，水煮，初吞四五枚，日三服，稍增至十五枚，旋煮旋吞，觉病减再作。忌羊肉、饧糖。此乃许仁则方也。【《外台秘要》】
