    Nausea and cold reversals, with phlegm inside: take one sheng of Banxia (Pinellia), wash, dry, and grind; one sheng of wheat flour, mix with water to make pill-sized balls, boil in water, initially swallow four to five balls, take three times a day, gradually increase to fifteen balls, boil and swallow again, feeling improvement in the condition. Avoid lamb and syrup. This is the prescription by Xu Renzhe.

    In the case of sudden death from corpse reversal, the pulse still moves; if faint whispers can be heard in the ears and eyes, and warmth is felt in the thighs, this is the sign. For death by nightmare, if one suddenly does not awaken, do not use fire to illuminate; instead, bite their heels and the area around the big toe nails, spit on their face to revive them, and also blow powdered calamus in their nose, and place powdered cassia under the tongue, along with administering the juice of calamus.

    If one has taken too many cooling medications resulting in cold extremities and weak pulse: use two and a half qian of dry beans, one and a half qian of powdered licorice, boil in two zhongs of water, then take one zhong.

    For phlegm reversal causing head pain like bursting: take thirty pieces of black plum flesh, three pinches of salt, and three sheng of wine, boil down to one sheng and take it all to induce vomiting, which will cure.

    For vomiting and cough with reversals: boil and drink the juice of疵藤.

    With wind and cold causing blockage of qi and blood, leading to painful coldness and numbness in the body and extremities: use two liang of Wulingzhi, one liang of myrrh, five qian of frankincense, and one and a half liang of processed Aconitum, ground into powder, form into small pills the size of bullets, taking one pill with warm ginger wine.[122p]

    　　卒死尸厥：用白马前脚夜目二枚、白马尾十四茎合烧，以苦酒丸如小豆大，白汤灌下二丸，须臾再服即苏。【《肘后方》】
    　　　　针灸

    　　《素问》曰：太阳脏独至，厥，喘虚气逆，是阴不足阳有余也，表里俱当泻，取之下俞。　　少阳脏独至，是厥气也，蹺前卒大，取之下俞。　　帝曰：有病膺肿，颈痛，胸满腹胀，此为何病？何以得之？岐伯曰：名厥逆。帝曰：治之奈何？岐伯曰：灸之则喑，石之则狂，须其气并，乃可治也。帝曰：何以然？岐伯曰：阳气重上，有余于上，灸之则阳气入阴，入则喑；石之则阳气虚，虚则狂。须其气并而治之，可使全也。寒气客于五脏，厥逆上泄，阴气竭，阳气未入，故卒然痛死不知人，气复反则生矣。寒气客于肠胃，厥逆上出，故痛而呕也。　　邪客于手足少阴太阴、足阳明之络，此五络皆会于耳中，上络左角，五络俱竭，令人身脉皆动而形无知也，其状若尸，或曰尸厥。[123p]

    If someone suddenly dies and appears as if in a state of rigor mortis: take two white horse front hooves and two night eyes, and burn fourteen stems from a white horse's tail. Prepare medicinal balls the size of small beans from strong wine, and administer two of these down with white soup. After a moment, if taken again, they will revive.

    Regarding acupuncture and moxibustion:

    The "Plain Questions" states: When the solar organ alone is affected, it leads to fainting and breathlessness due to excess yang and insufficient yin. Both the exterior and interior should be treated by purging from below. When the lesser yang organ is alone affected, it causes fainting gas. If there is sudden and severe pain, one should also purge from below.

    The Emperor asked: There is an affliction presenting with swelling, neck pain, chest fullness, and abdominal distension. What illness is this, and how does it occur? Qi Bo replied: This is called "fainting reversal." The Emperor asked: How should it be treated? Qi Bo replied: Moxibustion would lead to muteness, and stone treatment would lead to madness; it is necessary for the vital energy to be united for effective treatment.

    The Emperor asked: Why is this so? Qi Bo replied: When yang energy is excessively rising, it leads to an excess above; moxibustion directs the yang energy into the yin, causing muteness. Stone treatment depletes the yang energy, leading to madness. The treatment should be done once the energies converge to promote recovery.

    When cold energy invades the five organs, it causes fainting and upward leakage, resulting in depletion of yin energy. If yang energy has not entered, it can lead to sudden pain and death without awareness, but if the energy reverses, recovery is possible. Cold energy invading the intestines and stomach causes upward reversal, leading to pain and vomiting.

    Evil energy invades the pathways of the hands and feet, as well as the lesser yin, greater yin, and foot yangming channels. These five pathways all converge in the ear. When they are completely depleted, the body’s pulse moves while there is no awareness, resembling a corpse, which some refer to as "corpse fainting."[123p]

    刺其足大指内侧爪甲上去端如韭叶，后刺足心，后刺足中指爪甲上，各一痏，后刺手大指内侧去端如韭叶，后刺手心主少阴锐骨之端，各一痏，立已。不已，以竹管吹其两耳，鬄其左角之发方一寸燔治，饮以美酒一杯。不能饮者，灌之立已。　　《灵枢经》曰：阴刺者左右率刺之，以治寒厥，中寒厥，足踝后少阴也。　　刺热厥者，留针反为寒；刺寒厥者，留针反为热。刺热厥者，二阴一阳；刺寒厥者，二阳一阴。[124p]

    Insert the needle into the inner side of the big toe, at the base of the nail, where it resembles a leek leaf. Then prick the center of the foot, followed by the nail on the middle finger, with one insertion each. Next, insert the needle into the inner side of the hand's big toe, and then into the center of the palm, specifically at the tip of the lesser yin (Shàoyīn) points, with one insertion each. After this, if there is no relief, use a bamboo tube to blow into both ears. Take a square inch of hair from the left temple and burn it, then drink a cup of fine wine. If unable to drink, pour it down the throat immediately.

    The "Lingshu Classic" states: For yin needling, the left and right sides should be punctured accordingly to treat cold syncope and moderate cold syncope, with attention paid to the lesser yin behind the ankle. To treat hot syncope, leave the needle in longer as it counters cold; for cold syncope, leave the needle in longer to counter heat. To needle for heat syncope, there should be two yin and one yang; for cold syncope, the pattern shifts to two yang and one yin.[124p]

    所谓二阴者，二刺阴也；一阳者，一刺阳也。　　足少阳之别，名曰光明，去踝五寸，别走厥阴，下络足跗。实则厥，虚则痿躄，坐不能起，取之所别也。　　骨寒热者，病无所安，汗注不休，齿未槁，取足少阴于阴股之络。齿已槁，死不治。骨厥亦然。　　厥痹者，厥气上及腹，取阴阳之络，视主病也，泻阳补阴经也。颈侧之动脉人迎，人迎足阳明也，在婴筋之前；婴筋之后，手阳明也，名曰扶突；次脉，足少阳脉[足少阳脉：原作「手少阳」，据《灵枢》寒热病改。[125p]

    The so-called "two yin" refers to the two piercing yin; "one yang" refers to the one piercing yang. The divergence of the foot's lesser yang is called brightness, located five inches from the ankle, diverging to the jueyin and connecting to the foot's tarsus. When it is full, it leads to coldness; when it is deficient, it results in weakness and inability to rise from sitting, drawing from where it diverges.

    Regarding the cold and heat in the bones, the disease finds no rest, with incessant sweating and teeth not yet decayed; one should draw from the foot's lesser yin at the connection of the yin thigh. If the teeth have decayed, it is hopeless and cannot be cured. The same applies to bone coldness.

    For the condition of cold and blockage, the cold qi ascends to the abdomen; one should draw from the connections of yin and yang to observe the main ailment, to drain yang and tonify the yin channels. The artery at the side of the neck is called "renying," corresponding to the foot's yangming, located in front of the inguinal ligament; behind it, it is associated with the hand's yangming, named "futu." The next pulse is from the foot's lesser yang pulse.[125p]

    ]也，名曰天牖；次脉，足太阳也，名曰天柱；腋下动脉，臂太阴也，名曰天府。　　热厥，取足太阴少阳，皆留之；寒厥，取足阳明少阴于足，皆留之。　　厥逆为病也，足暴清，胸将若裂，肠若将以刀切之，烦而不能食，脉大小皆濇，暖取足少阴，清取足阳明。清则补之，温则泻之。　　厥逆腹胀满，肠鸣，胸满不得息，取之下胸二胁，咳而动手者，与背腧，以手按之立快者是也。　　热病头痛，颞颥目(疒挈)，脉痛善衄，厥热病也，取之以第三针，视有余不足。寒热痔[寒热痔：《灵枢》热病谓：「寒热痔，热病体重，肠中热，取之以第四针，……。」据此，寒热痔非厥热病之证，当删。]。　　厥挟脊而痛至顶，头沉沉然，目(目巟)(目巟)然，腰脊强，取足太阳腘中血络。　　厥，胸满面肿，唇漯漯然，暴言难，甚则不能言，取足阳明。　　厥气走喉而不能言，手足清，大便不利，取足少阴。[126p]

    The Heavenly Window is named for the primary channel; the next vessel, the Foot Shao Yang, is called the Heavenly Pillar; the artery under the armpit, the Arm Tai Yin, is named the Heavenly Mansion.

    For heat syncope, treat with the Foot Tai Yin and Shao Yang, keeping both; for cold syncope, treat with the Foot Yang Ming and Shao Yin in the feet, also keeping both.

    Syncope with reverse flow represents illness, manifesting as a violent chill in the feet, a feeling of the chest wanting to split, and the intestines feeling as if cut with a knife, causing vexation and inability to eat, with the pulse being thin and uneven. Warmth should be applied to the Foot Shao Yin, while clarity should be taken from the Foot Yang Ming. If the body is clear, supplement; if warm, drain.

    With reverse flow accompanied by abdominal distension, intestinal gurgling, fullness in the chest that obstructs breathing, apply treatment to the lower chest and both sides. If coughing leads to movement in the hands, and pressure applied yields immediate relief, that’s a positive sign.

    In cases of heat illness presenting with headaches, temporal pain, and aching eyes, if the pulse is throbbing with frequent nosebleeds, this is a heat illness. Treat with the third needle, observing for excess or deficiency.

    For cold-heat hemorrhoids, marked by weight in the body and heat in the intestines, treat with the fourth needle...

    When syncope causes pain extending to the spine and reaching the top of the head, with a heavy sensation in the head, and rounded eyes, and stiffness in the lumbar spine, treat the blood vessels of the popliteal fossa on the Foot Tai Yang.

    Syncope presents with chest fullness and facial swelling, with lips appearing parched and speech becoming difficult, even to the point of muteness; treatment should focus on the Foot Yang Ming.

    When the syncope energy travels to the throat, causing an inability to speak, with coldness in the hands and feet and difficulty in defecation, treatment should be directed at the Foot Shao Yin.[126p]

    　　厥而腹响响然，多寒气，腹中谷谷，便溲难，取足太阴。　　痿厥，为四末束悗，乃疾解之，日二，不仁者，十日而知无休，病已止。　　黄帝曰：何谓逆而乱？岐伯曰：清气在阴，浊气在阳，营气顺脉，卫气逆行，清浊相干。乱于臂胫则为四厥，乱于头则为逆厥，头重眩仆。有道以来，有道以去，审知其道，是为身宝。气在于头者，取诸天柱、大杼；不知，取足太阳荥输。气在于臂足，取之先去血脉，后取其阳明少阳之荥输。　　寒则地冻水冰，人气在中，皮肤致，腠理闭，汗不出，血气强，肉坚濇，当是之时，善用针者，亦不能取四厥。血脉凝结坚搏不往来者，亦未可即柔。故治厥者必先熨，调和其经，掌与腋肘与脚项与脊以调之，火气已通，血脉乃行，然后视其病脉淖泽者刺而平之，坚紧者破而散之，气下乃止，此所谓以解结者也。　　《甲乙经》曰：头重目瞑，凄厥寒热汗不出，陶道主之。　　肩髆间急，凄厥恶寒，魄户主之。[127p]

    When the limbs are cold and the abdomen makes a rumbling sound, there is much cold air; the abdomen is filled with gurgling sounds and it becomes difficult to urinate, involving the foot of the Taiyin. When limbs are weak and cold, with the four extremities bound, one must treat it accordingly, twice daily. If there is numbness, one will know within ten days that it has not ceased, and the illness will have stopped.

    The Yellow Emperor asked: What does it mean to be reversed and disordered? Qi Bo replied: Clear qi is in the yin, turbid qi is in the yang; nourishing qi moves smoothly through the vessels, while protective qi moves in reverse, with clarity and turbidity interfering with each other. Disorder in the arms and legs results in the four extremities being cold; disorder in the head leads to reverse cold and a heavy head that causes dizziness and fainting. With the right method and a way to resolve it, understanding this path is a treasure for the body.

    If there is qi in the head, it should be drawn from the Tian Zhu and Da Zhu points; if not understood, take the foot taiyang's Xingshu. If qi is in the arms and legs, first draw from the blood vessels, then from the Yangming and Shaoyang points.

    When it is cold, the ground freezes and water turns to ice; human qi is within, the skin closes, pores become blocked, sweat does not emerge, blood and qi become strong, and the flesh is firm and hard. At such times, even good acupuncturists cannot alleviate the four extremities' cold. When the blood vessels congeal and are firm, they cannot move freely; hence, one cannot soften them immediately.

    Therefore, to treat cold, one must first warm the area, harmonizing the meridians. Adjusting the palms, armpits, feet, neck, and spine to restore balance; once the fire qi flows, the blood vessels will circulate. Then assess the condition of the pulse; those that are muddy and stagnant should be needled and leveled, while those that are firm and tight should be broken up and dispersed until the qi settles, which is known as resolving the blockage.

    The "Neijing" states: A heavy head, closed eyes, cold sweat not flowing, indicate a need for the Tàodào master. If there is pressing pain between the shoulders and hips, cold sweat, and aversion to cold, the Po (soul) needs to be addressed.[127p]

    　　肩痛胸腹满，凄厥脊背急强，神堂主之。　　寒热凄厥，鼓颔，承浆主之。
    　　寒厥及热烦心，少气不足以息，阴湿痒腹痛，不可以食饮，肘挛支满，喉中焦干渴，鱼际主之。　　热病汗不出且厥，手足清，暴泄，心痛腹胀，心尤痛甚，此胃心痛也，大都主之，并取隐白。　　阳厥凄凄而寒，少腹坚，头痛，胫股腹痛，消中，小便不利，善呕，三里主之。　　厥四逆喘气满，风身汗出而清，髋髀中痛，不可得行，足外皮痛，临泣主之。　　四厥手足闷者，使人久持之，厥热 【一本作逆冷，】 胫痛，腹胀，皮痛，善伸，数欠，恶人与木音，振寒，嗌中引外痛，热病，汗不出，下齿痛，恶寒，目急，喘满，寒栗，断口噤僻，不嗜食，内庭主之。　　足厥喘逆，足下清至膝，涌泉主之。　　尸厥死不知人，脉动如故，隐白及大敦主之。　　恍惚尸厥烦痛，中极及仆参主之。[128p]

    Shoulder pain, fullness in the chest and abdomen, sharp stiffness in the back; the spirit hall governs these symptoms.

    Cold and heat, chill and convulsion, fullness in the jaws, and the承浆 (Chengjiang) governs these.

    Cold convulsions and hot agitation of the heart, insufficient breath, dampness causing itching and abdominal pain, making it impossible to eat or drink; elbow cramping, fullness, dryness and thirst in the throat—these are governed by the fish mound (Yujian).

    In cases of heat illness with no sweating and convulsion, cold hands and feet, explosive diarrhea, heart pain, and abdominal distention, especially severe heart pain—this is stomach heart pain, generally governed, along with hidden white (Yinbai).

    Yang convulsion with cold and chills, hardness in the lower abdomen, headache, pain in the legs and abdomen, digestive discomfort, difficulty in urination, tendency to vomit—governed by the three miles (Sanli).

    Convulsions and obstructed breathing with fullness, wind in the body, sweating yet feeling clear, pain in the hips and thighs causing inability to walk, and skin pain in the feet—governed by the tears weep (Linqi).

    For four convulsions with hands and feet feeling tight, sustained tension, heated in reverse, leg pain, abdominal distention, skin pain, good at stretching, frequent yawning—discomfort with men, wooden sound, shivering cold, a pain that pulls from the throat outward, heat illness, lack of sweating, pain in the lower teeth, aversion to cold, rapid eyes, fullness and shortness of breath, chills, closed mouth with tension, lack of appetite—governed by the inner court (Neiting).

    Foot convulsions with reverse breathing, cold feet up to the knees—governed by the springing source (Yongquan).

    In cases of corpse convulsions, unable to recognize a person, pulse pulsating as usual, governed by hidden white (Yinbai) and great tun (Dazun).

    In states of confusion with corpse convulsions and pain, governed by the center of extremes (Zhongji) and the seizing of the messenger (Puxin).[128p]

    　　尸厥暴死，金门主之。
    　　《千金方》曰：跗阳，主痿厥，风头重痛。　　《医学纲目》曰：身热如火，足冷如水，可灸阳辅穴。又云胻酸冷，绝骨取之。　　《医学入门》曰：尸厥百会一穴美，更针隐白效昭昭。外用笔管吹耳，不针百会，针上星亦同。　　《古今医统》曰：厥逆，灸人中一穴，在鼻下，灸七壮，或针入至齿妙。又膻中一穴，在两乳间陷中，灸二十壮。　　又法：以绳围臂腕，男左女右，将绳从大椎上度下，至脊中绳头尽处是穴，灸二十二壮愈。[129p]

    When a person dies suddenly, it is called "corpse qi."

    The "Qianjin Fang" states that for "fu yang," it is responsible for atrophy and convulsions, with severe pain in the head due to wind. The "Yixue Gangmu" mentions that if the body is hot like fire while the feet are cold like water, moxibustion should be applied to the Yangfu acupoint. It also notes that if there is coldness in the knee, treatment should involve the Qugu point.

    The "Yixue Rumen" states that for corpse qi, one should focus on the Baihui acupoint, which is particularly effective with needling at the Yinbai point. Additionally, blowing with a pen tube into the ear is suggested; needling Baihui is also effective, with similar results from needling at the Shangxing point.

    The "Gujin Yitong" explains that for reversal of qi, moxibustion should be applied to the Renzhong acupoint, which is located below the nose, with seven moxa sessions. Alternatively, needling to the teeth is also effective. The Xinde acupoint located in the depression between the two breasts should receive moxibustion for twenty sessions.

    Another method involves wrapping a rope around the wrist; men on the left, women on the right, taking the rope from the Daizui down to the middle of the spine, with the end point being the acupoint, applying moxibustion for twenty-two sessions to achieve healing.[129p]

    　　　　导引

    　　《保生秘要》曰：手足厥逆，法先念脐，次涌泉处，肋拔上至脐，又从脐处肋拔下至涌泉止，又从左手肋拔过右手，右手肋拔过左手，每次行六遍。
    　　　　医案

    　　《儒门事亲》曰：一夫病痰厥不知人，牙关紧急，诸药不能下，候死而已。戴人见之，问侍病者口中曾有涎否？曰：有。戴人先以防风、藜芦煎汤，调瓜蒂末灌之口中，不能下，乃取长蛤甲磨去刃，以纸裹其尖，灌于右鼻窍中，嘓然下咽有声，后灌其左窍，亦然。戴人曰：可治矣。良久涎不出，遂以砒石一钱又投之鼻中，忽偃然仰面，似觉有痛，斯须吐哕出胶涎数升颇腥。砒石寻常勿用，以其病大，非如此莫能动。然无瓜蒂亦不可便用，宜消息之。大凡中风涎壅，往往止断为风，专求风药，灵宝至宝，误人多矣。刘河间治风舍风不论，先论二火，故将此法实于火形中。[130p]

    Guidance

    The "Secrets of Preserving Life" states: When the hands and feet are cold and reversed, first focus on the navel, then on the Yongquan (bubbling spring) point. Pull from the ribs upwards to the navel, then from the navel downwards to the Yongquan, and finally from the left ribs across to the right ribs, and from the right ribs across to the left ribs, doing this six times each.

    Medical Case

    The "Righteous Way to Serve Parents" states: A man was ill with phlegm and syncope, not recognizing people, with tightly clenched jaws, unable to take any medicine, awaiting death. A practitioner saw him and asked if there was any saliva in the patient’s mouth. The answer was yes. The practitioner first prepared a decoction of Fangfeng and Lilies (zhilong), mixing it with powdered melon seed to administer orally. When that couldn’t go down, he took a long clam shell, ground off the sharp edge, wrapped the tip in paper, and applied it to the right nostril, hearing a sound as it swallowed. Then he did the same for the left nostril. The practitioner remarked: "He can be treated now." After a while, as no saliva came out, he then used one qian of arsenic and administered it through the nose. Suddenly the patient lay back, seeming to feel pain, and shortly thereafter spat out a large quantity of thick, fishy saliva. Arsenic should usually not be used; because the illness was severe, this was the only method to stimulate movement. However, without melon seeds, it should not be used casually, and care should be taken. Generally, for those suffering from phlegm obstruction due to stroke, people often mistakenly focus only on wind treatments, relying on ineffective wind medicines. Liu Hejian treated stroke by addressing fire first, thus applying this method effectively within the context of fire.[130p]

    　　西华李政之病寒厥，其妻病热厥，前后十余年。其妻服逍遥散十余剂，终无效。一日命予诊之，二人脉皆洪大而无力。政之曰：我手足之寒时时渍以热汤，渍而不能止；吾妇手足之热，终日沃以冷水，沃而不能已者，何也？予曰：寒热之厥也。此皆得之贪饮食，纵嗜欲。遂出《内经》厥论证之。政之喜曰：十年之疑，今而释然，纵不服药，愈过半矣。予曰：热厥者寒在上也，寒厥者热在上也。寒在上者，以温剂补肺金；热在上者，以凉剂清心火。分取二药，令服之不辍。不旬月，政之诣门谢曰：寒热厥者皆愈矣。[131p]

    Xi Hua's illness was a chill-induced collapse, while his wife's was heat-induced. For over ten years, she had taken Xiao Yao San with no effect. One day, she requested my diagnosis. Both had pulses that were large but weak. Xi Hua said, "My hands and feet are cold, and I soak them in hot soup, yet the chill does not stop; my wife's hands and feet are warm, and she soaks them in cold water, yet the heat does not subside. Why is this?" I replied, "It is a case of chill and heat-induced collapse. Both are the result of excessive eating and indulgence." I then referenced the "Inner Canon" to explain the condition. Xi Hua rejoiced, saying, "After ten years of doubt, I now understand. Even without taking medicine, I am already more than half healed." I said, "In heat-induced collapse, cold is above; in chill-induced collapse, heat is above. For cold above, use warming agents to tonify the lung; for heat above, use cooling agents to clear heart fire." I prescribed two medicines, urging them to continue taking them without interruption. Within a few months, Xi Hua came to express his gratitude, stating, "Both the chill and heat-induced collapses have been cured."[131p]

    　　《医宗必读》曰：社友韩茂远伤寒九日以来，口不能言，目不能视，体不能动，四肢俱冷，众皆曰阴证。比余诊之，六脉皆无，以手按腹，两手护之，眉皱作楚，按其趺阳，大而有力，乃知腹有燥屎也。欲与大承气汤，病家惶惧不敢进。余曰：吾郡能辨是证者，惟施笠泽耳。延至诊之，与余言若合符节。遂下之，得燥屎六七枚，口能言，体能动矣。彼按手不及足者，何以救此垂绝之证耶？
    　　给谏晏怀泉夫人，先患胸腹痛，次日卒然运倒，手足厥逆。时有医者以牛黄丸磨就将服之。余诊之，六脉皆伏，惟气口稍动，此食满胸中。阴阳痞隔，升降不通，故脉伏而气口独见也。取陈皮、砂仁各一两，姜八钱，盐三钱，煎汤以指探吐，得宿食五六碗，六脉尽见矣。左关弦大，胸腹痛甚，知为大怒所伤也，以木香、青皮、橘红、白朮、香附，煎成与服，两剂痛止。更以四君子加木香、乌药，调理十余日方瘥。此食中兼气中。[132p]

    "The Medical Book of Essential Reading" states: A friend, Han Maoyuan, suffered from a severe cold for nine days, unable to speak, see, or move, with all limbs cold; many declared it a shadow illness. Upon examining him, I found no pulse; pressing on his abdomen with both hands, I noticed his brow furrowed in distress. I pressed on the foot yang point, which was large and robust, indicating dried feces in the abdomen. I wanted to give him the Major Purge Decoction, but the patient was fearful and hesitant. I said: 'In our county, only Shi Lizhe can identify this condition.' After a delay, he was diagnosed by me and spoke as if he understood. I then administered the decoction, and he expelled six or seven pieces of dried feces, regaining ability to speak and move. How could those who only checked the hands, not the feet, rescue him from this critical condition?

    I treated Lady Yanhua Quan, who initially suffered from chest and abdominal pain and suddenly collapsed the next day, with cold hands and feet. A physician had prepared a cow bile pill for her to take. Upon examination, I found her pulse deep, but the qi at the mouth slightly moved, indicating food stagnation in the chest. With yin and yang blocked, and ascent and descent obstructed, the pulse was hidden while qi was somewhat observable. I took one tael of dried orange peel and sand seeds, eight qian of ginger, and three qian of salt, decocting them for a finger probing and inducing vomiting, resulting in five or six bowls of food being expelled, revealing the pulse completely. The left guan pulse was large, and the chest and abdominal pain was severe; I knew it was caused by great anger. I prescription wood incense, green peel, tangerine skins, white atractylodes, and cyperus, decocting and prescribing; with two doses, the pain ceased. I then used the Four Gentlemen Decoction plus wood incense and black myrrh, adjusting the treatment for over ten days before she fully recovered. This involved both food stagnation and qi stagnation.[132p]

    　　吴门周复庵年及五旬，荒于酒色，忽然头痛发热，医以羌活汤散之，汗出不止，昏运不醒。余与之灸关元十壮而醒，以四君子加姜、桂日服三剂，至三日少康。又因分析家产，劳而且怒，复发厥。余用好参一两，熟附二钱，煨姜十片，煎服稍醒，但一转侧即厥。一日之间，计厥七次，服参三两。至明日以羊肉羹糯米粥与之，尚厥二三次。至五日而厥定。向余泣曰：已蒙再生，不知有全愈之日否？余曰：脉有根蒂，但元气虚极，非三载调摄不能康也。幸其恪信余言，遵守用药，两月之间服参四斤，三年之内进剂六百贴，丸药七十余斤，方得步履如初。亲友众多，议论杂出，若非病人任之专，或久而见疑，服药少怠，未有获生者也。[133p]

    In the Wu Gate, Zhou Fu'an, at the age of fifty, was indulging in wine and pleasure. Suddenly, he experienced headaches and fever. The doctor treated him with Qianghuo Decoction, resulting in continuous sweating and a loss of consciousness. I applied moxibustion on his Guan Yuan point ten times, and he woke up. I prescribed the Four Gentlemen Decoction augmented with ginger and cinnamon for daily consumption, and by the third day, he showed signs of recovery. However, when he began to analyze his estate, the exertion and anger caused a relapse. I used one and a half taels of good ginseng, two qian of熟附 (prepared Rehmannia), and ten slices of cooked ginger, which slightly revived him, but he would faint again upon turning. In one day, he experienced seven fainting spells, consuming three taels of ginseng. The next day, I gave him mutton soup and glutinous rice porridge, yet he fainted two or three more times. By the fifth day, the fainting spells stabilized. He wept to me, saying: "I have already received rebirth; I wonder if I will fully recover?" I replied: "Your pulse shows a rooted vitality, but your vital energy is extremely deficient; it will take three years of care and adjustment for you to truly regain health." Fortunately, he faithfully heeded my words and adhered to the medication. In two months, he consumed four pounds of ginseng, and within three years, he took six hundred doses of medicine and over seventy pounds of pills, until he was able to walk as before. His many family and friends voiced various opinions, but if not for the patient’s sole commitment to the treatment, or if there had been any lingering doubts, or if there had been any negligence in taking the medicine, few would have achieved recovery.[133p]

    　　《薛氏医案》曰：一男子食少胸满，手足逆冷，畏寒发热，吐痰，饮食时欲作呕，自用清气化痰及二陈、枳实之类，胸腹膨胀，呕吐痰食，小便淋漓。又用四苓、连、蘗、知母、车前，小便不利，诸病益甚。余曰：此脾胃虚寒无火之证，故食入不消而反出。遂用八味丸补火以生土，用补中益气加生姜、桂培养中宫，发阳气，寻愈。
    　　大司马王浚川呕吐宿滞，脐腹痛甚，手足俱冷，脉微细，用附子理中丸一服益甚。脉浮大，按之而细，用参附汤一剂顿愈。

    The "Medical Cases of the Xue Family" states: A man experienced fullness in his chest after eating little, with cold hands and feet, a fear of cold and a fever, and he was spitting phlegm. During meals, he felt nausea and used remedies like Qingqi Huatan and Erchen, as well as bitter orange, which caused his chest and abdomen to swell, resulting in vomiting of phlegm and food, with dribbling urination. He then used Sifeng, Lian, Banxia, Zhimu, and Cheqian, but his urination did not improve, and his condition worsened. I said: This is a case of weak spleen and stomach with cold and no fire, hence food cannot be digested and is regurgitated. I then used Bawei Pill to tonify fire and generate earth, added ingredients like ginger and cinnamon to support the center and stimulate Yang Qi, leading to recovery.

    Great General Wang Jun experienced vomiting of accumulated food, severe abdominal pain, cold hands and feet, and a weak pulse. He took a dose of Fuzhong Wan which significantly helped. His pulse became floating and large, but weak upon pressure; using Shenfu Decoction, he improved rapidly.[134p]
